1935.06.29

Fengtai Riot Erupts: Rebels Attack Peiping but are Repelled; Insurgents Bomb Yongdingmen; Dispersed After Pursuit by Garrison Troops; Traffic Between Peiping and Tianjin Restored; City is Calm and Peaceful; Rebels Said to be Former Subordinates of Bai Jianwu and Shi Yousan; Military Council Held Meeting Yesterday to Discuss Security Issues 1

(Peiping) This morning, the people of Peiping suddenly heard booming cannon fire, causing panic. Afterwards, the inner and outer cities of Peiping remained closed, preventing vegetable vendors from entering the city. Residents faced great difficulty purchasing vegetables in the early morning. The prices of oil, salt, and other goods in the streets and alleys rose sharply, and rice shops tripled their profits. No trams left the depot this morning, there were few rickshaws, and few pedestrians. Many shops also did not open, resulting in a desolate scene. Traffic was temporarily cut off at Xuanwumen, Hepingmen, Zhengyangmen, Chongwenmen, Tiananmen and other places in the southern city. Newspaper delivery men, vegetable vendors, and rickshaw pullers were completely stopped outside the city, and were only allowed to pass around 10:00 AM, which slightly calmed the people. Few students arrived at the city's elementary schools until noon, resulting in an unofficial holiday. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) After the sound of cannon fire was heard in Peiping this morning, military police, and other relevant parties were prepared for local security and strengthened the alert. Therefore, order prevailed. The rebels launched the attack from the Fengtai area, threatening armored vehicles and advancing towards Peiping. At the Nan Quekou (South Breach) area outside Yongdingmen, they were intercepted by military police and security forces and immediately retreated towards Fengtai. After being pursued by military police, the bandits in the Fengtai and Yongdingmen train station areas were completely cleared by 10:00 AM this morning, and the situation was restored to normal. A remnant of the bandits abandoned their vehicles and fled eastward across the Baihe River. Our infantry and cavalry units are currently dividing up to intercept them. After the incident occurred, the Peiping local authorities held a meeting all night in a certain location and have devised thorough and stable measures for Peiping's security. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) Military dispatch: Around 1:00 AM this morning, several cannon shots were suddenly heard in Peiping, coming from the south. After investigation, it was found that a small group of rebels in Fengtai suddenly attacked our armored vehicle unit, seized the armored vehicles parked there, and forced them to fire towards Yongdingmen, intending to enter the city through the Nan Quekou (South Breach) in the outer city. Our garrison troops at that location intercepted them head-on. The rebel troops were unable to advance and retreated to Yongdingmen train station. Subsequently, our officers and soldiers went out of the city to suppress them. The rebel troops at that location have fled towards Fengtai. The Yongdingmen area has been completely restored to its original state. As for the bandits in the Fengtai area, they have been routed by our troops and are fleeing towards the war zone. Our troops are currently in pursuit. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) After 8:00 AM this morning, pedestrians were allowed to pass through the streets and traffic was restored. All shops opened and resumed business as usual. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) A total of seven cannon shots were heard inside the city this morning. One landed at the Hongwen Apartment in Dongjingjidao, one on the earthen mound in Erlongkeng, one at the former Jingjidao Art Academy, and one at No. 25 Baozi Street, none of which exploded. The whereabouts of the other two shots were not determined. The local military, police, and gendarmerie authorities are jointly maintaining order in Peiping, ensuring safety. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) Locations where cannonballs landed this morning: (1) Four iron balls with a diameter of five fen landed in the Hongbin Apartment in Dongjingjidao. Another large ball blasted a large pit one or two chi long and one chi deep in front of the north-facing room's door. (2) A pit about two chi wide and deep was blasted on the mound in front of No. 10 Shanggangmen. (3) Two relatively large iron balls landed at the former Jingjidao Art Academy, knocking down a piece of brick from the flower window of the lower floor. (4) An iron ball landed in front of the south-facing room's door at No. 31 Shoupa Hutong. (Special dispatch, 11/18)

(Peiping) After the incident outside Yongdingmen was quelled this morning, police inspection revealed three people struck by stray bullets: Li Wenfu and Jia Wanchun, both injured and sent to the municipal hospital for treatment. There was also one dead person whose name is unknown. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) An official announcement stated that around 1:00 AM this morning, plainclothes soldiers in Fengtai attacked and seized an armored vehicle, forcing the driver to drive it towards Peiping. The soldiers guarding the city resisted. The rebel troops eventually retreated to Fengtai. The rebel soldiers in Fengtai have now been routed and have fled into the demilitarized zone. Five cannonballs landed in the city. The military police are maintaining order in Peiping, and there is absolutely no danger. (Reuter's dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) The Japanese military authorities here are currently consulting with commanders of foreign troops to discuss joint actions in the event that the Peiping disturbance spreads. A Japanese spokesperson here stated today that the Japanese do not consider this matter to be serious. The Peiping-Tianjin Railway has been suspended for some time, and the Blue Steel Train has also been unable to run. Telephone communications at the Fengtai Station were cut off last night but are currently being repaired. There are rumors here that an armored vehicle came from Peiping to Tianjin. It is unknown whether this vehicle belongs to the rebel troops, and the public is quite worried. (Reuter's dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) Peiping implemented a sudden curfew at 11:00 PM on the 27th, cutting off all traffic in the city. The reason given was that Bai Jianwu, a former subordinate of Wu Peifu, was commanding 2,000 bandits in an attempt to seize Peiping by force, but this plan was exposed before it could be realized. (Japanese United Press dispatch, 28th)

(Nanjing) At noon on the 28th, the military authorities here received a telegram from Peiping reporting that at around 1:00 AM on the 28th, when the 10th parcel train on the Beijing-Hankou Railway arrived at Fengtai Station, over a hundred plainclothes bandits with short guns got off the train. Taking advantage of the crowd of passengers, they rushed into the armored vehicle of the 6th squadron stationed at Fengtai Station, claiming to be organizing a "North China State" with Bai Jianwu as the commander-in-chief of the Righteous Autonomous Army. At the same time, they coerced the armored vehicle unit to fire five cannons at Yongdingmen in Peiping (one shell exploded in the air, four did not explode, and none injured anyone). The Peiping garrison immediately dispatched troops to meet and severely attack them. The bandit troops were unable to withstand the attack and retreated towards Fengtai. Our armored vehicle unit and infantry then cooperated to track down and suppress them. By 11:00 AM, all the bandits in the Fengtai area had been defeated and fled eastward. There were no traces of bandits in Fengtai. Traffic between Peiping and Tianjin was restored this afternoon. Peiping is calm and peaceful as usual. The city and outside are under extremely strict guard, and security can be ensured. (Central News Agency dispatch, 11/18)

(Peiping) The course of the plainclothes bandit disturbance in Fengtai on the evening of the 27th, according to investigations, is as follows: The 6th Squadron of armored vehicles was originally stationed in Fengtai to maintain railway traffic. Some of the officers and soldiers within were reorganized from Shi Yousan's former railway protection force. Because the officers were mostly in Peiping and no one supervised them, the bandits took the opportunity to launch a surprise attack. In addition to sending 30-40 people to sneak into Fengtai beforehand, the remaining 80-odd people arrived at Fengtai on the 10th train from Tianjin on the evening of the 27th. At 0:40 AM on the 11/18, they seized the armored vehicles. At the time, the soldiers were cooling off under the vehicles, caught off guard, and were seized by the bandits, forced to drive the vehicles and fire cannons, and advance towards Yongdingmen, intending to enter through the breach in the outer city. The bandits all had the words "Pseudo Righteous Autonomous Army" wrapped around their left arms. The Peiping Public Security Bureau received a telephone report from Fengtai at 12:00 AM after the vehicle moved, and immediately notified the military, police, and gendarmerie authorities, dispatching military police to suppress them. At the same time, a temporary curfew was announced throughout the city. At 1:15 AM, the bandits forced their way into the outer city, and our defending soldiers intercepted them head-on. The bandits were unsuccessful and retreated to Yongdingmen Station. Half an hour later, our officers and soldiers went out of the city to suppress them. The bandits, realizing the disparity in numbers, fled back to Fengtai. At this time, our officers and soldiers, fearing that the bandits would return, had no choice but to dismantle a section of the railway south of Yongdingmen Station to prevent the bandits from advancing. By dawn on the 28th, the officers and soldiers had again scattered the remaining bandits in Fengtai, killing more than 20. There were still 50-60 people who fled eastward from Fengtai, intending to harass the area south of Tongxian and around Yanjiao. Our army is currently dispatching teams to pursue and suppress them. When the bandits were causing trouble in Fengtai, they cut off the railway bureau's telegraph and telephone lines, temporarily cutting off communications. Peiping's security relied on the effective maintenance of order by the military, police, and gendarmerie, and remained peaceful as usual. Wang Shuchang, Shao Wenkai, Yuan Liang, and Yu Jinhe all stayed up all night, personally directing operations, and sandbags were placed at all important locations for strict security. The curfew was lifted and the situation restored to normal only after receiving reports at 9:30 AM on the 28th that the bandits had been defeated. Traffic between Peiping and Tianjin was restored in the afternoon. The Military Council held an emergency meeting at 8:00 AM on the 28th, attended by Bao Wenxue, Hu Yukun, Ji Yiqiao, Qin Dechun, Xiao Zhenying, Wang Shuchang, etc., where they discussed maintaining security. After the meeting, they sent telegrams to President Wang, Chairman Chiang, and Acting Chairman He, reporting on everything. Yuan Liang also telegraphed the capital detailing the course of events. According to a certain authority, the number of bandits was small and they have been scattered by the officers and soldiers. In addition to ordering constant vigilance, Peiping's security is absolutely guaranteed, and merchants and residents can remain calm. (Central News Agency dispatch, 11/18)

(Tianjin) Japanese military staff officer Omaki Yoshihisa visited Shang Zhen, the commander of the Tianjin Garrison Security Headquarters, on the 28th to discuss security issues in Tianjin. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) At 9:00 AM this morning, order was fully restored in Peiping. Most shops opened as usual. The gates of the inner city were opened around 9:00 AM, and the gates of the outer city, except for Yongdingmen, were allowed to open to traffic around 10:00 AM. All government offices and banks conducted business as usual. After the disturbance occurred, all traffic on the Peiping-Shenyang section of the Beijing-Shenyang Railway was suspended. Westbound trains stopped at Langfang, and eastbound trains were not dispatched, resulting in a desolate scene at the platforms. The 41st Peiping-Shijiazhuang train on the Beijing-Hankou Railway, which departed at 7:00 AM this morning, returned to the West Station due to the closure of the city gates. The 1st Peiping-Hankou special express train at 10:20 AM has departed on schedule. Long-distance telephone service between Peiping and Tianjin is operating normally. The Beijing-Shenyang Railway dispatched a track inspection train around 1:00 PM this afternoon to explore the route. It is hoped that traffic can be restored this afternoon. The train to Tongzhou, scheduled to depart at 1:40 PM this afternoon, has departed on schedule. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) The leader of the Fengtai incident was Bai Jianwu, the former division commander of the Zhili Army, who claimed to be the commander-in-chief of the Righteous Autonomous Army. The plainclothes bandits he recruited were all former subordinates of Liu Guitang and Shi Yousan, as well as Wang Zizhen's unit, Shi Yousan's nephew. After their defeat, they did not disperse but fled to Yanjiao and went into hiding. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) On the morning of the 28th, due to the Peiping-Tianjin railway tracks being cut, the Peiping-Pukou train No. 306 had already reached Langfang and returned to Tianjin. The 302 Peiping-Shanghai through train, the 2nd Peiping-Shenyang through train, the 6th Peiping-Liaoning express train, and the 42nd Peiping-Liaoning slow train were all blocked and stopped at Tianjin Main Station. Until the railway tracks were repaired in the afternoon, trains 306, 2nd, and 42nd were separately opened to Peiping at 2:45 PM, 3:10 PM, and 3:40 PM. The 1202nd and 6th passenger and freight trains were attached to these 2nd trains. The remaining trains departed at their original times. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) There are no more traces of bandits in Fengtai, and traffic between Peiping and Tianjin will be restored immediately. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) Wang Shuchang, the commander of the Peiping-Tianjin Garrison, said that a bandit disturbance was discovered last night in the Fengtai area, threatening the armored vehicle unit stationed there. They were driven off head-on by the dispatched military police, and they are currently being surrounded and suppressed in the Fengtai area, which can be resolved completely. Proper measures have been planned for Peiping's security, and there is absolutely no problem. The curfew will be lifted as soon as the incident is quelled. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) The 726th Regiment of the 141st Division of the 32nd Army, stationed in Liangcheng, is responsible for security in Haixia, Xian Shuigu, Chen Tangzhuang, and other places. Although people felt uneasy all day on the 28th, the city situation was particularly peaceful. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) After the Fengtai incident occurred, in order to maintain the safety of the city and local security, a curfew was announced today, and a curfew headquarters was established, with Wang Shuchang as the curfew commander and Shao Wenkai as the deputy commander. Starting at 9:00 PM, pedestrians will be inspected. The security of Peiping is the responsibility of the military, police, and gendarmerie and can be expected to be safe. Military and police agencies are stepping up their guard. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) Shang Zhen said on the 28th that the Fengtai rebels were jointly suppressed by two regiments of Miao Zhengliu's division, and the cavalry team of his own division. Around 12:00 PM, those who retreated to Fengtai abandoned their vehicles and scattered in Huangshipo, and were also surrounded and routed. They are currently being pursued by various units. Peiping declared the lifting of the curfew that afternoon, and there is absolutely no cause for concern about the security of this city. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) Huang Shipo Gu, the stationmaster of the Beijing-Shenyang Railway, reported that at 12:50 PM on the 28th, he was kidnapped to Nanyuan by a group of bandits. The number of bandits was less than 200. They were defeated in Huangcun, and when they fled, they were extremely disheveled, fleeing from Nanyuan to Tongzhou and then to Yanjiao, Sanhe. The empty armored vehicle cars are currently parked at Huangcun Station. The Huang Shipo stationmaster has been released and has returned to Huangcun. At 1:00 PM on the 28th, a track maintenance train departed from Fengtai to repair the damaged railway tracks between Wanyizhuang and Huangcun. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) The 6th Squadron of armored vehicles belonging to the Direct Jurisdiction Military Council is stationed in Fengtai, with the task of protecting the railway. The families of the officers and soldiers all live in the city. Before the incident last night, at 9:00 PM, more than 100 bandits boarded a train from Tianjin, all with white bands wrapped around their inner sleeves. After arriving in Fengtai, they disembarked there. At 12:40 AM, they attacked the 6th Squadron's armored vehicles stationed there. Because there were fewer soldiers on the vehicles, they were unable to resist for a time, and the vehicles were seized by the bandits. After seizing the vehicles, the bandits posted slogans there, calling themselves the Righteous National Salvation Autonomous Army. At the same time, they forced the vehicles to drive towards the city. At 1:05 AM, the vehicle arrived at the South Breach of Yongdingmen. When the vehicle left Fengtai, the Peiping Public Security Bureau received an emergency report and immediately telegraphed the garrison stationed there to stand by. When the vehicle arrived at the South Breach, the iron shed gate had already been closed. The bandits forced the guards to open the gate, and a melee began. The bandits fired three cannons first, then seven more, for a total of ten shots. When the cannons were fired, the telegraph and telephone lines between Peiping and Fengtai were cut by the bandits, and several sections of the railway tracks were also excavated. In the evening, in order to prevent trouble, the city of Peiping remained under curfew from 10:00 PM. Traffic between Peiping and Tianjin, the Peiping-Shanghai through train, and all other trains were fully restored from 3:05 PM this afternoon. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) News of the Fengtai incident arrived in Tianjin on the morning of the 28th, and the authorities here immediately mobilized police teams to strengthen security. People's hearts are still at ease. After the Peiping-Pukou train No. 106 returned from Langfang, it departed from Tianjin to Peiping at 2:40 PM. The Peiping-Shenyang through train also arrived in Tianjin from Peiping at 5:00 PM in the afternoon. In addition, all stations in Tianjin implemented a curfew at 8:00 PM on the 28th, with increased security at all important roads. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) The temporary curfew order in Peiping was lifted at noon on the 28th. However, rumors abound, and people's hearts are wavering. It was only after learning that Bai Jianwu's troops had been repelled by Shang Zhen's troops tonight that peace was restored in the city. (Electric News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) Tianjin is under special curfew from 9:00 PM tonight due to the influence of Peiping. (Electric News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) Peiping was suddenly attacked by rebel bandits last night. How many rebels were there? What were their aims? Who was in command? It is not yet possible to ascertain these things. There was booming cannon fire at night, and cannonballs landed in the streets, giving the capital the appearance of being besieged. There was fighting in various parts of Peiping, the most prominent being near Yongdingmen, where the troops and security forces bravely resisted the rebels. The armored vehicles possessed by the rebels advanced along the southwest city and fired cannons at the defending soldiers. It is reported that one civilian was killed by cannon fire. At that time, all twelve city gates of Peiping were closed and barricades were set up for defense, and a curfew was announced with traffic completely suspended. Last night's disturbance began in Fengtai, which is on the Peiping-Hankou line, seven miles from Peiping. Approximately 350 to 2,000 rebels occupied Fengtai Station and advanced towards Peiping. Outside Yongdingmen, the troops under Wan Fulin refused them entry, and the two sides opened fire, with cannon fire erupting intermittently. At 7:30 AM, armored vehicles formerly belonging to Yu Xuezhong but recently transferred to Wan Fulin arrived from Fengtai and bombarded the defending troops. The defending troops retaliated with mortars, machine guns, and rifles. The defending troops at the South Gate used mortars to destroy the railway tracks under the armored vehicles, and the armored vehicles advanced along the west city, firing into the city. After the fighting started, the Peiping authorities immediately mobilized reinforcements and dismantled the railway tracks between Peiping and Fengtai to cut off the armored vehicles' route of advance and retreat. The rebel troops were repelled and retreated towards Fengtai. The rebel troops wanted to defend Fengtai Station, leading to fierce fighting for several hours, but they were eventually surrounded by Shang Zhen's troops. The rebel troops then surrendered. At noon, Peiping lifted the curfew. It is reported that a mutiny has occurred in Tongzhou, a demilitarized zone. There are also reports of disturbances in Changxindian. The Peiping rebels clearly acted according to a predetermined plan, first attacking the South Gate because there were railway tracks running through it. Railway traffic between Peiping and Tianjin is temporarily completely suspended. Opinions differ on who is in charge of this rebellion. Some say that the rebels are led by a certain officer formerly under Wu Peifu, but the commander of the South Gate garrison said that the rebels there were commanded by Shi Yousan. The capital is currently like a dead city, with all traffic suspended and a curfew in effect. Banks, shops, and schools are all closed. The Japanese military authorities have stated that this is purely an internal Chinese affair and that there is no reason to interfere at present, but if the disturbances spread, the Japanese will have to take steps to protect Japanese residents. Planes from the Kwantung Army frequently circled over Peiping during the day, and approximately 300 guards from the Japanese legation gathered in the legation barracks to prevent incidents. (Reuter's dispatch, 11/18)

(Tianjin) Liu, the supervisor of the Fengtai Station factory, reported to the Beijing-Shenyang Railway Bureau that at 11:20 PM on the night of the 27th, the Peiping-Shenyang train No. 20 arrived at Fengtai. Many bandits got off the train and occupied the station, cutting off traffic. Personnel were assigned to guard the telephone exchange. Some of the soldiers of the 6th Squadron of armored vehicles stationed at the station joined forces with the bandits. The bandits demanded armored vehicle locomotives from the factory, but because the boilers were being cleaned, they could not be fired up. The bandits then forced the opening of the factory's No. 324 locomotive to tow armored vehicles to Peiping. Gunfire and cannon fire were then heard in the distance. At 9:00 AM, they retreated without stopping, and then drove to Huangshipo. They stopped outside the station to the north. The bandits changed into plain clothes and kidnapped the Huang Shipo stationmaster. At 11:40 AM, the commander of the armored vehicle unit, Cao Yaozhang, chased after them on the 5th squadron's armored vehicle. By noon, order had been restored in Fengtai. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) This morning, a certain division in our city was urgently ordered to cooperate with the defending soldiers at the South Breach to jointly surround and attack the bandits, so the bandits did not succeed. When the division was mobilized, the troops stationed in Nanyuan also received orders to advance north, intercepting the bandits' rear. The standoff lasted until dawn. Because the bandits were attacked from both sides, and because the Nanyuan army had completely dug up the railway tracks between Yongdingmen and Fengtai, the bandits once retreated to the station outside Yongdingmen. Later, because our army surrounded and attacked them, by 9:00 AM this morning, the bandits abandoned the armored vehicles and fled on foot towards Fengtai. At this time, the commander of the armored vehicle corps also led armored vehicles to assist. Because our army advanced quickly, the bandits abandoned the armored vehicles of the 6th Squadron, which were recovered by our army without damage. When the bandits retreated in disarray towards Fengtai, they carried more than sixty bodies that had been killed in the vehicles. The rest fled eastward from Fengtai, currently fleeing towards the border area of Tongxian and Sanhe. Officers and soldiers are currently dividing up to search. At 9:30 AM, our army completely recovered Fengtai, and is currently out searching for and suppressing them. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) Long-distance telephone service between Peiping and Tianjin was temporarily interrupted on the morning of the 28th. From Tianjin, it was only possible to speak to Fengtai, and even then the connection was intermittent. The Peiping-Tianjin telegraph line was not damaged, and the volume of telegrams was extremely heavy. (Special dispatch, 11/18)

(Tianjin) According to sources in the communications authorities, the Fengtai incident occurred at 8:00 PM on the night of the 27th, when more than 200 plainclothes bandits boarded the Peiping-Shenyang slow train No. 24 from Tianjin, mixed in with ordinary passengers. At 11:20 PM, when the train arrived at Fengtai, the bandits got off the train, removed their plain clothes, revealing white shirts and blue pants, and with the symbol of the Righteous Autonomous Army wrapped around their arms. They seized the vehicles of the 5th and 6th squadrons of armored vehicles stationed at the station. The commander of the 6th Squadron was a former subordinate of Shi Yousan and coerced his subordinates to be accomplices, and the bandit troops occupied it. At 1:00 AM, they drove the vehicles towards Peiping to attack Yongdingmen. Until noon on the 28th, they were attacked from the front and rear by the Miao Zhengliu and Song Kentang divisions. The bandit troops were unsuccessful and drove back to Fengtai. Without stopping, they retreated to Huangshipo, unloaded heavy machine guns and other weapons from the vehicles, and fled towards Tongxian and Yanjiao. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) Shang Zhen said that the Fengtai incident involved two armored trains stationed there. One part of armored vehicle went to Peiping for disturbance, and another part conducted disturbances in Fengtai. There were more than 200 bandits in total. Afterwards, they were surrounded and suppressed by the Miao's brigade, the Lu and Liu regiments, and the cavalry battalion of the 32nd Army. It was resolved at noon, and the bandits abandoned their vehicles and fled far away towards Tongzhou. Post-incident matters will be handled by the Military Council. There is no cause for concern about the security of Tianjin, and the military and police have been working together to strictly prevent incidents. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) Yin Tong, the director of the Beijing-Shenyang Railway Bureau, who is currently convalescing at Beidaihe due to illness, telegraphed the railway bureau to inquire about the truth of the Fengtai incident after hearing about it on the 28th. (Special dispatch, 28th) Empty rooms in the East Legation Quarter are now fully rented and occupied.

(Peiping) Peiping's security has now been fully restored, which is due to the local authorities' swift response. The overall situation was settled in the afternoon, the curfew order was lifted, and most of the city gates have been reopened. The reasons for the disturbances are rumored to be varied. When the armored vehicles drove to the west city, they fired fragmentation shells into the city. Fortunately, the residents were mostly asleep, and there were few deaths or injuries. This afternoon, a Japanese spokesman stated that the Japanese authorities were quite satisfied that the Chinese authorities had quelled the disturbances and would therefore not take any action. The official quarters are now denying the claim that the rebels were subordinates of Wan Fulin. According to reliable sources, when the army recovered the armored vehicles at 11:00 AM this morning, they observed that there were many weapons in the vehicles that had never been seen before, including 55 five-centimeter Mitta light cannons and three machine guns. This afternoon, one plainclothes soldier was arrested outside the Peiping Municipal Government, carrying three handguns. After interrogation, he admitted that there were a total of 300 plainclothes soldiers hiding in various parts of the city. Therefore, the authorities have decided to reissue the curfew order, prohibiting pedestrians from 8:00 PM tonight. (Reuter's dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) More than 30 plainclothes soldiers have sneaked into the war zone. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Peiping) The approximately 2,000 bandits commanded by Bai Jianwu, a former subordinate of Wu Peifu, have retreated eastward after being attacked by Wan Fulin's troops. Also, the armored vehicles that attempted to invade the city through Yongdingmen late on the 27th fled northwest after being attacked by Shang Zhen's troops and the security forces at 9:30 AM on the 28th. (Electric News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) Zhang Haijiao's gang, the former Old Mouse's troops from Qingshankou outside the Great Wall, engaged in fierce fighting with the Japanese puppet joint forces on the 26th. Zhang's bandit gang claimed to be the "Manchu-Mongolian Autonomous National Salvation Army" and posted slogans everywhere saying that they would not disturb the people. Cao Yao, the commander of the armored vehicle corps, arrived at Fengtai from the Peiping-Suiyuan Railway on the 28th by armored vehicles to search for the bandits. Passenger trains between Peiping and Tianjin accelerated through the Huangshupo-Fengtai area as a precaution. Mail between Peiping and Tianjin was interrupted for a day and was restored on the evening of the 28th. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Efforts Following the Reduction of Export Taxes 2

— End

The Customs Export Tariff. In order to reduce or eliminate export taxes, a major revision has been made and was announced on the 25th of this month. As a result of this revision, animal products have largely benefited from tax reductions. Marine fish and shellfish, fresh and dried fruits, are entirely tax-free. Vegetables, vegetable oils, and peanuts and raw kernels have also been reduced in tax. Furthermore, metals, which accounted for 5.74% of the total value of exports last year, are now tax-free, with the exception of yellow, purple copper and tin ingots. There are even more exemptions in the miscellaneous goods category. The vast majority of what this newspaper previously hoped the authorities would implement in terms of reduction and exemptions (see March 27, 24th year, editorial) has now been realized. It is estimated that there are 41 items with reduced taxes and 87 tax-free items. Adding to the original 38 tax-free items, there are now a total of 125 tax-free export items. It can be said that, apart from the occasional one or two uniquely produced in our country that are still taxed, the majority of export goods have benefited from reductions and exemptions.

At a time when the country's finances are difficult, the government has taken this measure, although it cannot be implemented immediately, but its painstaking efforts to protect industry and commerce should be seen by the people of the country. Moreover, the reason why it cannot be implemented immediately is, as Minister Kong said, "... once abolished, before a definite compensation is determined, revenue will inevitably be greatly affected. The government must pay attention to relieving industry and commerce on the one hand, and to balancing income and expenditure on the other. It should be implemented immediately after the compensation has been properly prepared." This is because there is no temporary remedy in finance. It is believed that the way to raise compensation is to either implement fair new taxes or reorganize existing tax revenues. However, the only way to compensate is still to increase import tax rates to increase import tax revenue to make up for the loss of reduced or eliminated export taxes. The trend is smooth, and it also fully protects domestic agriculture, industry, and commerce. It is also a path taken by all countries internationally, so there is no need for hesitation.

Some argue that strict tax barriers are common in countries around the world today. However, China's situation is unique, and there is often a feeling of hidden restrictions. For example, the changes in the tax regulations for cotton goods and marine products in the 23rd year were also to comply with the requests of friendly nations. If this situation does not change, increasing import taxes will face many obstacles. Moreover, there are still mutually beneficial agreements on some items. Even if there are increases in the future, I am afraid there will not be many. Increasing or decreasing tariffs is a country's internal affair. If country A levies heavy taxes on country B's imports, country B only has one way to retaliate with retaliatory taxes. For example, recently, because Canada increased import taxes on Japanese goods and levied other tariffs in addition to the ordinary import tax, the Japanese only responded by levying an ad valorem import tax of 50% on eight items imported from Canada, including lumber, wheat, flour, and pulp. (See the 26th-day Japan United Press dispatch). It is not heard that there are any other actions besides this. This shows that changes in commodity tax rates, except for agreed-upon tariffs, are beyond the intervention of others. Moreover, even if there are changes in China's import tariffs, it is for the sake of self-survival and is different from Canada's taxation, which contains exclusive characteristics. There is no reason to invite foreign objections.

However, although our country's export taxes have not been completely abolished, they have been gradually reduced and exempted. Therefore, if there is a solution for finance, I know that the government will definitely not hesitate to completely eliminate these export taxes. The only thing that the government can benefit industry and commerce is protection. Now that export taxes have been largely reduced and exempted, how will our industry and commerce promote their products overseas? This is the responsibility of industry and commerce itself. In the past, although speakers have been earnest about the failure of the export business, what have industry and commerce done to improve themselves? Now that the national crisis is destroying everything and foreign goods are dumping more fiercely, our industry and commerce are in a more difficult situation and bear greater responsibilities. If they still follow old ways and seek only small immediate gains, without considering the greater difficulties of the future, then their greatest achievement will only be a foreign goods seller begging for leftovers. Therefore, how to develop the export industry in the future depends on each industry thoroughly examining past failures and what others do better than us. On the one hand, unite various industries related to exports to fight together overseas. On the domestic front, establish close contact, and have the determination to seek survival in desperate situations, with an unwavering spirit. Other parties should also do their utmost to help the export business, with sympathetic supervision. In order to maintain the credibility of export goods, the same industry should conduct strict inspections to prevent inferior goods from being sold in abundance to protect our foreign credibility. As for those handled by the state, it is hoped that the procedures will be simple, the handling will be swift, and the fees will be low. If constant efforts are made by all parties in this way, there may be hope for a turnaround in foreign exports.

Guo Taiqi's Important Speech at the All-England Peace Conference: Urgently Stating the Necessity of Maintaining Political Morality Internationally; A Strong and Powerful China Is a Solid Tower for World Peace 3

(London) Chinese Ambassador to London Guo Taiqi delivered a speech at the 25th meeting of the All-England Peace Conference here today, emphasizing the importance of political morality and international integrity for the world, especially for China. The meeting was chaired by the famous British politician Henderson, with many foreign representatives in attendance. In his speech, Ambassador Guo stated that the close contact between countries has never been as close as it is today, and the mutual rejection has never been as great as it is today. China's construction of the Great Wall was justified, at least it was used to reject ancient barbarism. However, the tariff and quota barriers of the new era, and the suspicion and interrogation of entrants, only seek to close the country to reject their own kind, and develop the appendages of barbarism. One trend that can be detected today is that the conclusion of treaties is only to conceal aspirations. Its clear words can be ingeniously cancelled without damaging credibility. Concluding treaties is a way to secure peace, and its general dignity has not been slightly reduced, it is not correct to say this. China is probably the most victimized, but the institutions of international peace have been broken. Maintaining the health of international political life does not lie in concluding more treaties, its only condition lies in respecting all our treaties. Fundamental democracy and political philosophy are the same in China and Britain. In Chinese history, its brilliance is often diminished, but it can always be restored in time. Ambassador Guo then elaborated that although the Chinese government has encountered unprecedented difficulties, it has not relaxed its efforts in national construction. He said, "We Chinese especially regard Sir Rose's visit to China as a sincere manifestation of Britain's willingness to cooperate with China in technical matters." Ambassador Guo then asked the audience to read Wang Jingwei's "The Chinese Question and Its Solution," and concluded by saying that what China needs is respect for its sovereignty, independence, and integrity. China's needs are also the needs of the whole world. A strong and powerful China is a solid tower for world peace. (Reuter dispatch, 28th)

British Public Opinion Tested: Peace Vote Results Announced 4

More Than 10 Million People Participated in the Vote; Supporting the League of Nations and Supporting Disarmament

(London) The League of Nations Association held a conference at Albert Hall today. Representatives of various political parties, Chinese Ambassador Guo Taiqi, and other diplomats attended the joint platform. Viscount Cecil announced the results of the "Peace Vote" on the League of Nations, disarmament, and the international control of armaments. A total of 11.5 million people participated in the vote. More than 11 million votes supported Britain remaining a member of the League of Nations, with only 356,000 votes against. Approximately 10.5 million votes supported uniform reductions in armaments under international control, with only 862,000 votes against. Approximately 10.5 million votes also supported banning the manufacture of weapons for profit, with 775,000 votes against. As for the question of whether to implement economic and non-military sanctions against aggressor countries, 10 million votes were in favor, with 635,000 votes against. Only 6.75 million votes supported the implementation of military contributions, with 2.351 million votes against. Speakers included Canterbury Archbishop Lamb, Archbishop of the City Noehut, International Women's Suffrage and Equal Citizenship Alliance President Mrs. Ashebi, and Trade Union Congress Secretary-General Sir Citrine. When two of the speakers praised Cabinet Minister Eden's efforts to promote peace in Europe, cheers arose one after another. This can be regarded as one of the highlights of the meeting. A woman serving in the labor community delivered a speech petitioning for mothers who were victims of the war, and many listeners were moved to tears. Dr. Noehut said, "People's hearts are the same. The majority of people in all countries of the world must feel the same as us." The audience also responded with cheers. Viscount Cecil declared that there are very few bright spots in the international community. One of them is that Britain's support for the League of Nations is more serious and clear than before. He hoped that the results of this vote could show the world that it can now rely on Britain's support for the collective security system. Afterwards, the meeting passed a resolution urging the government to implement a policy of peaceful construction and universal disarmament. Only one person voted against it, and the crowd shouted "Expel him!" "Expel him!" endlessly. (Reuter dispatch, 27th)

The Japanese Army's Toyama Unit: 10,000 Troops Transferred to the Northeast 5

Osaka: The Japanese Army's 9th Division, led by Division Commander Toyama, boarded two military vessels from Kobe to the Northeast at 7:00 AM and 9:00 AM this morning. The number of troops is approximately 15,000. (China United Press dispatch, 28th)

The New League of Nations Building Is Nearing Completion: The Original Meeting Place Is Up for Auction 7

(Geneva) The new League of Nations building, the Ariana Palace, will be completed soon, and the relocation is imminent. The original meeting place has been used for fifteen years and has now been put up for auction. Secretary-General Avenol has requested cooperation from all member states and is widely promoting it. The Swiss government has suggested that if no one is willing to purchase the building for 4 million Swiss francs or more, the Swiss government guarantees to purchase it for this amount as state property. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

Completing His Eastern Mission: Eden Returns to London; Italy's Ambitions in East Africa Increase the Severity of the European Situation 8

Consultation on British and French Opinions Still Needs Reconciliation; Hoare to Issue a Statement in the British House of Commons

(London) Minister without Portfolio Eden, after visiting Paris and Rome, returned here by plane tonight. At the airport, he issued a statement saying, "I am very happy to return to the country after visiting the capitals of France and Italy. However, regarding the mission completed during this trip, I will submit a report to the Cabinet and cannot announce anything. What I can say is that the talks with the French and Italian governments were conducted in a spirit of utmost sincerity." When a reporter asked if he planned to go to France again in the near future, Eden replied, "I don't know about this. I will first report the results of this trip to my Cabinet colleagues. In short, everything must be left to fate." (Havas dispatch, 27th)

(London) British Foreign Secretary Hoare will issue a statement in the House of Commons today regarding Minister without Portfolio Eden's travels to Paris and Rome. (Reuter dispatch, 28th)

A foreign affairs correspondent for the Daily Telegraph stated that, in light of the Italian-Abyssinian conflict, the current European situation is in an unpredictable state. The European collective peace system is likely to be completely destroyed within a few months. Eden's trip to Rome has fully demonstrated that Mussolini is unwilling to take any solution other than conquering Abyssinia by force. If Britain insists on interfering, Italy will not hesitate to withdraw from the League of Nations. (National Telegram, 28th)

British and French Differences Not Fully Resolved 9

(Paris) British Minister without Portfolio Eden returned to the country by plane at 7:45 PM. He had a brief meal with Premier and Foreign Minister Laval at a restaurant at noon, but did not continue the conversation. In the afternoon, Laval accompanied Eden to the Chamber of Deputies to observe the meeting. This morning, Eden and Laval discussed methods to implement the various issues proposed at the Stresa Conference, but there were still no results. It is heard that the British Cabinet decided yesterday to request the French government to put forward new proposals, but Eden has not yet received this instruction. Generally speaking, Britain has always agreed with the suggestions in the Anglo-French London Declaration of February 3, but insists that individual issues should be resolved through bilateral agreements whenever possible. France, on the other hand, has always insisted that the procedures proposed at the Stresa Conference should be resolved simultaneously. According to informed sources, France does not oppose the question of the Skyoggano Convention being discussed before other issues, but with one condition: that the existing links between the Sky Convention, the Eastern European Convention, the Danube River Convention, and land armaments issues must be strictly maintained. After Eden returns to the country, Anglo-French negotiations will continue through diplomatic channels. The British side hopes that the differences between the two sides can be reconciled soon. Regarding the Abyssinian issue, it is heard that Eden only briefly notified Laval of the situation of his talks with Mussolini, without putting forward any suggestions to Laval. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

(Paris) British Minister for League of Nations Affairs Eden arrived here from Rome and, after meeting with Premier Laval again, flew back to London today. It is generally believed that the results of Eden's trip are mixed. However, the detailed content of his talks with French Premier Laval and Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has not been fully disclosed. It is impossible to rashly draw a final conclusion based on the brief press releases. At 1:30 PM today, Laval announced to the press the results of his talks with Eden, "Sir Eden returned from Rome and told me the content of his discussions with Prime Minister Mussolini. We have studied good methods to resolve the issues within the scope of the London Protocol of February 3 and are working hard to achieve it. We are now deciding to continue the review through diplomatic channels because of the short time and the inability to deliberate at length. We have the same feeling and determination to adjust the methods we use and promote the plan of February 3. As for the Abyssinian issue, Eden also told me the content of his discussions with Mussolini." Before leaving, Eden went to the French House of Deputies at the afternoon meeting and sat in the diplomatic seat to listen. Then he met with Laval again in the cabinet room. (National Telegram, 27th)

The Door to Franco-German Negotiations Is Open 10

Berlin Attaches Importance to Laval's Statement

(Berlin) Laval's mention in the Senate Foreign Affairs Committee that the door to Franco-German negotiations is now open has attracted considerable attention from Berlin newspapers. The Berlin Daily News believes that Laval's wording is too solemn and considers it not only a probe to Germany but also a probe to Britain. The newspaper then mentioned Britain's attitude, stating that when Laval asked Britain what attitude it would take towards Anglo-French cooperation, Britain replied with reserved independent action. It can be seen that although Britain and France cooperate in the future, it is parallel in nature, not a complete policy of commonality. (National Telegram, 27th)

British Newspaper Commentary Expresses Disappointment 11

(London) Newspaper commentary on Eden's trip to Paris and Rome is mostly disappointed because there are no very definite results. Although they want to cover it up, they are unable to do so. The Daily Mail's Paris dispatch stated that although Eden's talks with Laval cannot be said to have made no progress, the main issues have not been resolved. However, The Times believes that Eden's trip has at least one achievement, that Laval is no longer as opposed to France and Germany holding direct talks as before. Therefore, Germany's plan to send Ribbentrop to France to discuss disarmament issues may not be rejected again. (National Telegram, 28th)

The Black-Clad Prime Minister's Insatiable Desire 12

(London) According to the Daily Telegraph, Britain has proposed to Italian Prime Minister Mussolini to revise the northern border of Abyssinia, so that the coastal area of Abyssinia's Artiga province can be incorporated into Italian colonies. It is also heard that the Emperor of Abyssinia is preparing to hold a joint conference with France, Italy, and Britain to negotiate a solution to satisfy part of Italy's hopes. Abyssinia is willing to grant Italy the convenience of exploiting its mineral resources, but is unwilling to give up Abyssinia's political independence. To compensate for Abyssinia's losses, Britain is willing to cede a part of British Somaliland as a "corridor" for Abyssinia to reach the Red Sea. However, Mussolini did not agree to take Britain's proposal as the basis for negotiations. According to the Daily Telegraph, Italy's minimum demand seems to be to annex most of Abyssinia's territory and place the entire country under Italian protection. Italy's demands are very different from Britain's proposals, so the negotiations are completely deadlocked. The newspaper also said that if the League of Nations opposes Italy's plan to annex Abyssinia, Italy will inevitably withdraw from the League of Nations. (Havas dispatch, 26th)

The King of Abyssinia Denounces Italian Military Actions 13

Abyssinian Capital: King Salassie of Abyssinia strongly condemned Italy's determination to control Abyssinia and its plan to reduce it to a protected status today. A statement was issued by the Foreign Office, criticizing Italy's continuous increase in troops to East Africa and stating that if Abyssinia needs foreign officers, it can appoint them itself. Abyssinia cannot accept any strong country forcing it to hire foreign officers. (National Telegram, 28th)

If Something Happens in Europe, Italy Is Prepared; The Army Is Preparing for Large-Scale Maneuvers; Military Budget Increases Sharply 14

(Rome) According to the People's Daily, "The government will soon hold large-scale army maneuvers to show that although a large number of Italian troops have been sent to East Africa, there is still sufficient powerful military force in the country to defend the motherland in case of an event in Europe."

(Rome) The government issued an order to increase the army budget by 61,789,000 lire and the navy budget by 34,022,00 lire. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

The Work of the Italian-Abyssinian Arbitration Committee Seeks to Find the Responsibility for the Dispute; The Future Is Undoubtedly Difficult 15

The Hague: The Italian-Abyssinian Joint Arbitration Committee issued a communiqué after continuing its meeting at the Scheveningen Grand Hotel this morning, stating that the committee has taken the necessary preparations to allow representatives from both Italy and Abyssinia to present their statements to the committee. Therefore, the governments of both Italy and Abyssinia will probably send representatives here. The representative sent by Abyssinia is Professor Sis, a legal advisor at the Abyssinian embassy in France and a professor at the University of Paris. Someone asked a member of the committee, who replied that the committee's work is to specifically seek the responsibility for the Italian-Abyssinian dispute. The member did not conceal that the future of the work is fraught with difficulties. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

(London) According to a message from the capital of Abyssinia in the Daily Telegraph, the Abyssinian government recently issued a communiqué stating that Italy is continuing to send troops to East Africa, in numbers far exceeding what is needed to defend its territory. The Abyssinian government is still not preparing for mobilization. The Italian-Abyssinian Joint Arbitration Committee is meeting in Scheveningen, the Netherlands. If Italy is justified, Abyssinia will definitely satisfy it. The Emperor of Abyssinia has previously requested the League of Nations to appoint neutral members to investigate the actual situation on the ground and submit a report. The communiqué does not deny that the slave system still exists in Abyssinia, but states that progress has been made in the work of liberating slaves, and that other reforms are underway. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

Mussolini Attaches Importance to Agriculture and Participates in Threshing Work 16

(Rome) During the threshing season in the Littoria Province, Prime Minister Mussolini made a special trip to the newly built villages and farms in the province's Porgu Basutia and Sapodia this morning to participate in the work, showing his importance to agriculture. He took off his coat and engaged in threshing for three hours. Afterwards, he went to the tenant registration office to sign and receive wages. Then he delivered a speech to the farmers, saying, "At this moment, we are all good farmers, and in the future, we will be good soldiers." His excited atmosphere was overflowing, and the listeners were moved. Littoria Province was transformed from marshes by the Fascist Party government in 1932 through a huge project. The province has a total area of 1,600 hectares, with 355 kilometers of roads and 1,480 kilometers of canals. There are a total of 2,167 farms and 19,29 households. The harvest this year is estimated to be 140,000 quintals, of which wheat accounts for 100,000 quintals. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

French Naval Chief Criticizes the Anglo-German Agreement; The Wartime National Organization Bill Is Submitted to the French Chamber of Deputies for Discussion 17

Brest: Naval Chief Pittly mentioned the newly concluded Anglo-German naval agreement today and strongly criticized Britain, saying that the problem is unfortunately one of the bears. For France, it must now consider the tonnage of the British navy. This move was not necessary in the past, but now the situation is very different. Pittly also asked whether Britain had observed its traditional caution in concluding this agreement. (Reuter dispatch, 27th)

(Paris) The government drafted a legal draft for "Wartime National Organization," which was approved by the Supreme National Defense Council and has now been submitted to the Chamber of Deputies for opposition. The purpose of this law is to be able to use all the resources of the country in the shortest possible time in the event of war. The intention of this law is to establish a legal basis for the relationship between the state and private individuals in wartime. If a friendly agreement cannot be reached between the state and private individuals, the state can forcibly conscript. The law also stipulates that all French men and women over the age of 18 must be forced to serve the country in wartime, but the state will pay them wages. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

Italian-French Military Liaison: The Chiefs of Staff of the Two Countries Meet in Rome 18

(Paris) According to a Rome dispatch from the Morning News, French Chief of Staff General Gamolin arrived in Rome on Quantity III to discuss liaison methods with the Italian General Staff. General Ge met with Italian Chief of Staff General Balbo yesterday, and visited Prime Minister Mussolini in the afternoon. (National Telegram, 28th)

The British Government Plans to Convene a Naval Conference This Autumn, Will Begin Seeking Opinions from Various Countries, and the General Election Will Be Postponed to Next Spring 19

(London) A Reuters parliamentary correspondent learned that the British general election, originally scheduled for October, now appears to be postponed until next year. In addition to the heavy legislative agenda, including a new unemployment bill, it is reported that the government will soon begin seeking opinions from various countries in the hope of convening a naval conference this autumn, with London as the venue. Therefore, the general election seems likely to be held in early next year. (Reuters dispatch, 28th)

(Washington) Today, when asked whether he supports British Prime Minister Baldwin's proposal for Anglo-American naval cooperation or alliance, Naval Secretary Swanson did not directly answer, but said that this was entirely a matter for the State Department and Congress, and the Navy Department had no right to make decisions on its behalf. However, Swanson also stated that so-called cooperation would only be effective in wartime, and when war came, the United States would welcome any assistance that could help it win. (National dispatch, 27th)

(London) Regarding the negotiations for convening a naval conference in October of this year, although the British side is working hard to proceed, it now seems to have reached a deadlock. Germany is unwilling to immediately submit a detailed plan for its naval shipbuilding program. Germany's intentions regarding its navy are quite ambiguous, especially concerning aircraft carriers. According to German newspaper reports, Germany plans to build two aircraft carriers, which has caused considerable anxiety among British officials. The Anglo-German Naval Agreement stipulates that Germany can exceed the 35% ratio for submarine construction, to the point of being equal to Britain. The intention of this provision was to have Germany divert the tonnage of aircraft carriers to the construction of submarines. Now, there is widespread fear that Germany will still build aircraft carriers, creating a new situation in the naval issue, and then demand an increase in the submarine ratio. It is rumored that if Britain allows Germany to immediately begin building submarines, Germany may not build battleships before the expiration of the Washington Treaty in 1936. In addition, the preparatory negotiations between the British government and France, Italy, and the Soviet Union regarding the naval conference have encountered significant difficulties. Therefore, it is doubtful whether the naval conference can be held at the time proposed by Britain. Britain recently invited naval experts from France, Russia, and the United States to hold preliminary naval talks in London in the near future. However, the French side replied that if France participated in these talks, public opinion would consider France to have tacitly approved the Anglo-German Naval Agreement. The Italian government indicated that it would need a considerable period before it could send experts to London. The Soviet Union also took a similar reserved attitude and expressed opposition to Sweden increasing its Baltic Sea fleet, saying that since the Anglo-German Naval Agreement had been established, the only way to guarantee the safety of the Baltic Sea was for Britain to allow respect for the neutrality of the Danish Straits (the straits connecting the Baltic Sea and the North Sea) in wartime. Therefore, it can be seen that even the preliminary expert talks may be difficult to hold. It is also rumored that Britain has proposed that if the naval conference is held in October of this year, the following issues should be included on the agenda: (1) If the total naval tonnage cannot be regulated by ratios between countries, at least the maximum limits should be set for the tonnage and gun caliber of various classes of warships. (2) Each country attending the naval conference should allow each other to notify the governments of other countries of their naval shipbuilding plans within six years and agree not to change these planned shipbuilding programs within six years. However, in some democratic countries, governments often change, and political strategies are also frequently revised, making it difficult to avoid changing shipbuilding plans within six years. This is also a difficulty facing the future of the naval conference. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

Germany Actively Constructing Highways 20

(Berlin) The highway stretching 1,500 kilometers from Frankfurt to Darmstadt was just completed and opened to traffic in late last month, and the highway from Berlin to Stettin (at the mouth of the Oder River on the Baltic Sea coast) will also be completed within days. It can be seen that the government's highway construction project is now progressing rapidly. It is reported that the construction of this road is a massive project, not only erecting two 225-meter-long bridges over the Oder River, but also filling in many swamps with 2 million cubic meters of sand to ensure the stability of the roadbed. (Havas dispatch, 28th)

Haas Gives Speech in France on China's Construction Achievements: The Government Authorities Are Pragmatic, and Even Young People Focus on Practice 21

(Paris) The Institute of Pacific Relations, founded by the late General Maurice Bourquin and others, has been in existence for four years. The committee has invited famous people to give speeches on Far Eastern issues more than fifty times. Notable examples include Maurice Morel, Deputy Director of the International Labour Office, and Professor Escarra of the Faculty of Law at the University of Paris, advisor to the Chinese government, who have all given lectures. Today, the committee held a meeting and invited Haas, director of the Communications Section of the League of Nations, to give a speech. Haas spent a long time in China. His last trip was as a liaison officer between the League of Nations and the Chinese Economic Committee, on a mission to China for two months. He described in detail the various efforts of the Chinese government in construction, saying that the authorities all embraced pragmatism, and young people were also not focused on theory but inclined towards practice. China is progressing very quickly in material terms, such as: (1) Highways, which are well-built, comfortable to travel on, and have no accidents along the way. He himself traveled 1,500 kilometers on these highways. Cars and buses traveling on the highways must pay road tolls to cover road maintenance costs. Provincial officials are currently studying the construction of bridges and the use of charcoal-powered vehicles for transportation. (2) Railways. (3) Industry, especially in Shanxi and Guangdong, is the most developed. He visited leather and wool factories in Shanxi and sugar refineries in Guangdong. (4) Water conservancy. The authorities spare no effort in managing various rivers, especially the irrigation projects in the Northwest. (5) Agriculture. Haas was deeply impressed by the influence of the cooperative movement on rural life and organization in China, which attracted the attention of the audience, saying that there is a general trend towards the application of scientific methods in rural areas everywhere. As for rural health issues, government offices have established health bureaus everywhere. Once established, villagers flock to them, vying to be first, and the results have been very good. Haas concluded by saying that the various reforms he witnessed in China proved that work in various economic fields has deeply penetrated the bottom of society. (Havas dispatch, 27th)

Severe Rainstorms in Northern Kyushu, Japan, Cause Disaster for Days 22

Shimonoseki: The torrential rain in the northern Kyushu area gradually stopped at noon on the 28th. The rainfall actually reached 178 hao (equivalent to 3 shi and 1 dou and 3 sheng per ping), breaking the 175 hao of Taisho 12 (1923), making it the heaviest rainfall in thirteen years. (Japan United Press dispatch, 28th)

Fukuoka: Since the continuous heavy rains in the northern Kyushu and Yamaguchi Prefecture areas, 5,000 houses in Kurume City have been flooded, and the military has been mobilized to impose martial law. 2,000 houses in Yamaguchi City have been flooded, and hundreds of houses in other ports have also been flooded. Agricultural products have been severely damaged, and transportation facilities such as railways have also been disrupted. The rainfall in northern Kyushu did not stop until 6 p.m. today. (China United Press dispatch, 28th)

Legislative Yuan Passes Budget Compensation Measures, Approves Temporary Suspension of Four ILO Conventions, Returns Vocational Introduction Law for Review, and Passes Sichuan Public Debt Regulations and Bankruptcy Enforcement Law 23

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan held its 23rd plenary session on the morning of the 28th, with 65 members including Jiao Yitang in attendance. Sun Ke presided, and Liang Hancao served as secretary-general. The following matters were discussed: (1) Civil Servant Performance Appraisal Law; (2) Civil Servant Performance Appraisal Rewards and Punishments Regulations; Resolution: Both were passed as reviewed by the Legal System Committee. (3) Amendment to Article 10 of the Supreme Court Organization Law; Resolution: Passed as reviewed by the Legal System Committee. The Chief Secretary of the Supreme Court will remain a recommended appointment, without promotion to simplified appointment. The article does not need to be amended. (4) Bankruptcy Enforcement Law Drafted by the Civil Law Committee; Resolution: Passed as presented. The law contains six articles. The most important is the provision of Article 149 of the Bankruptcy Law, which stipulates that events of inability to pay debts that were completed before the implementation of the Bankruptcy Law are not applicable. Those who were declared bankrupt before the implementation of the Bankruptcy Law may apply for restoration of rights in accordance with the law. The Provisional Regulations on Debt Settlement for Merchants will become invalid after the implementation of the Bankruptcy Law. In addition, it is planned to set October 1 as the implementation date of the law, and it will be submitted to the National Government for approval. (5) Convention on the Employment of Women for Night Work; (6) Convention on Compensation for Occupational Diseases of Workers; (7) Convention on the Regulation of Working Hours in Automatic Glass Factories; (8) Convention on Guaranteeing Compensation and Allowances for Workers Forced into Unemployment; Resolution: All four of the above cases were passed as reviewed by the Foreign Affairs and Labor Law Committees and should be temporarily suspended from ratification. As for the Vocational Introduction Law, although the Legislative Yuan had completed the second reading process, the chairman believed that the case contained many foreign legal codes and neglected the national conditions of the country, so it would be nothing more than a formality after promulgation. For the sake of caution, he advocated that it should be returned for review. The motion was unanimously passed, and Shi Weihuan, Lou Tongsun, Shi Shangkuan, Lin Bin, Luo Ding, and Wei Tingsheng were designated as reviewers for the case, to be convened by Shi Weihuan. Subsequently, a closed-door meeting was held to deliberate on the Sichuan Reconstruction Public Debt Regulations and the Ministry of Finance's plan to compensate for the shortfall in revenue and expenditure in the 23rd year of the Republic (1934) general budget. It is reported that the results have been passed as presented. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance, based on the debt revenue of 50 million yuan listed in the revenue of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934) general budget, has decided to issue 100 million yuan in customs revenue public debt to compensate for the shortfall in revenue and expenditure in the 23rd year of the Republic (1934) and to recover the 50 million yuan in treasury bonds originally issued. The relevant regulations were passed by the Legislative Yuan on the 28th and will be issued on June 30. (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Nanjing) The formal fundraising measures formulated by the Ministry of Finance for the debt funds originally listed in the temporary revenue category of the national general budget for the 23rd year of the Republic (1934) are now known to be nothing more than issuing public debt. For a long time, the Green Ministry of Finance has planned to issue public debt based on the regulations in the national general budget for the 23rd year of the Republic (1934) to offset bank interest loans. However, it is still difficult to raise a large amount of funds. After repeated planning by the Ministry, it was only possible to draw out a portion of the short-term treasury bond funds issued in recent years to guarantee the new debt, so as not to increase the burden of tax rates, and the new debt could also be issued. As a result, the Central Government approved the issuance of public debt to exchange a portion of the 50 million yuan face value of the customs treasury bonds for the 23rd year of the Republic (1934), returning bank interest loans, which is also used to compensate for the shortfall in revenue and expenditure in the national general budget for the 23rd year of the Republic (1934). The interest rate on the new debt is 6% per annum, with interest paid quarterly every three months. The debt term is ten years, and the principal and interest will be fully repaid by June 30, 1945. The face value is issued at 98, divided into three types: 5,000 yuan, 1,000 yuan, and 100 yuan. The Central Bank is designated to pay principal and interest. The public debt regulations were approved smoothly at the Legislative Yuan meeting on the 28th. The name and amount of the debt will not be announced by the Ministry of Finance before issuance. (Central News Agency dispatch, 28th)

Permission to Use Machine-Assisted Hanging for Executing Death Sentences in Prisons 28

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Justice ordered the high courts of all provinces, stating that Article 466 of the new Criminal Procedure Law states that the death penalty shall be executed in prison, but there are no explicit regulations on the method of execution. After considering the situation in various regions and various methods of execution, hanging is still the preferred method. Hanging is divided into machine-assisted and manual methods. All prisons should uniformly use machines to ensure simplicity, kindness, and speed, and should use anesthesia methods as far as possible at the time of execution to reduce the suffering. However, before machines are purchased, manual hanging methods will still be used. In addition to submitting a report to the Judicial Yuan for record, the ministry should instruct all prisons to comply. (Special dispatch, 28th)

After Resolving the Chahar Incident, Ambassador Arita Issues Statement 34

(Local News) Ambassador Arita issued a statement at 11:00 a.m. today (the 28th) regarding the North China and Chahar issues. The contents are recorded below: (1) The continued occurrence of the North China and Chahar incidents prompted the Japanese Imperial military authorities to make fair demands on the Chinese military authorities based on the Armistice Agreement. It is fortunate that the Chinese military authorities have accepted these demands, leading to an improvement in the situation. We also hope, as expected in the statement of the commander of the Japanese army stationed in China, that the Chinese side will increase its efforts to maintain peace in that area. This is our earnest hope.

(2) In order to achieve a complete reconciliation of the relations between Japan and China, we believe that it is necessary to eliminate the anti-Japanese sentiment throughout China, not just in one place. However, to this day, that sentiment has not been completely eradicated. At this juncture, we should promote the full implementation of the order for good neighborly relations promulgated by China and hope to make further efforts to ban anti-Japanese sentiment. This is our earnest expectation. (Japan United Press dispatch, 28th)

(Tianjin) The commander of the Japanese army stationed in China issued a statement at 11:00 a.m. today regarding the North China and Chahar incidents, saying that the Chinese side has already promised to implement the Japanese army's fair and just demands regarding the issue of illegal activities by some Chinese officials and civilians in North China and Chahar Province. This is fortunate, and we acknowledge their sincerity and plan to temporarily observe the state of their implementation and await the improvement of the situation. The demands made by the Japanese army in this negotiation are based on the regulations of the Armistice Agreement, the oath of the Sino-Japanese military and police to punish those responsible for violating the agreement, to eliminate the source of trouble, to rebuild trust, to maintain peace, and to remove the threat to "Manchukuo" and the obstacles to Sino-Japanese friendship. Any deliberate expansion of the situation or interference in China's internal affairs is definitely not something we have ever considered. Sino-Japanese friendship and cooperation are what Japanese civil and military officials earnestly desire, but this cannot be achieved through superficial formalities or rhetoric. Considering the deep-rooted origins of the unfortunate incidents that have occurred this time, we deeply regret it. However, the Chinese government recently reissued a proclamation prohibiting anti-Japanese and anti-foreign activities throughout the country and has taken a step forward in eliminating the aforementioned source of trouble, which is admirable. The Japanese army hopes that the Chinese authorities will eliminate all anti-Japanese and anti-Manchukuo activities in various aspects of the region. This is our statement. (Japan United Press dispatch, 28th)

(Tokyo) The Ministry of the Army issued a statement in the form of a discussion on the main points of the important statement issued today by Commander Umezu of the Japanese garrison army in China. The gist of the statement is as follows: The statement by the commander of the Japanese garrison army in China is not only the opinion of the army stationed there but also fully coordinated with the central army headquarters, indicating the general intention of the army. The disposal of North China in the future is all contained in this statement. We hope that the harmonious relationship between China and Japan will be realized in a substantial and concrete way. In order to hope that the friendly relationship will be permanent, the resolution of the North China situation is particularly desired. (Dentsu dispatch, 28th)

Chen Yi Arrives in Nanjing from Shanghai 40

(Nanjing) Accompanied by three adjutants, Chen Yi arrived in Nanjing by train from Shanghai at 7:00 AM on the 28th. Representatives of Director Wang, including Chen Rui, Huang Musong, Cao Haosen, Lin Wei, and dozens of former subordinates from the military department, were all present at the station to welcome him. After alighting from the train, Chen Yi entered the city by car and rested at the Lizhi Society. It was arranged for him to meet with Director Wang and Minister He at noon on the 28th. Chen Yi spoke to reporters in detail about the administration of Fujian Province, briefly stating that he had been in Fujian for one year and five months and that the provincial situation urgently needed to be reported to the central government in detail. Therefore, he made a special trip to the capital. After the remnants of bandits in Fujian fled westward from Jiangxi, the large groups were gradually eliminated, and the local area was declared stable early on. Sporadic appearances of three to five scattered bandits are not a cause for concern. Regarding the administrative situation in recent years, last year was dedicated to stabilizing local affairs, and this year, we began organizing the work, actively rectifying local administration. For example, in the past, the collection of land taxes in various counties had no "fish scale" records to verify, and no one knew how much was collected. After the reorganization, taxes are now collected according to the register, so that every penny goes to the public, and the people are spared the suffering of excessive levies. Also, in the past, when county magistrates were replaced, county government personnel would leave with them. Now, county government officials do not change with the removal or replacement of the county magistrate. In addition to the reorganization, we are also supplementing with investigation and research this year, which is expected to be completed by the end of this year, and construction work can begin next year. The financial situation was originally extremely chaotic in the past. Although reorganization began last year, it was greatly affected by the brief incursion of Jiangxi bandits into Fujian, resulting in a budget deficit of one million yuan in the 23rd year. Measures are now being taken to make up for this in the 24th year budget. I will stay in the capital for about a week before returning to Fujian. It is not yet decided whether to go to Sichuan. (28th Central News Agency)

(Nanjing) Chen Yi visited He Yingqin in the afternoon of the 28th and also visited friends in the capital. At 4:00 PM, he went to Director Wang's official residence in the Ministry of Railways to report on the situation in Fujian Province. He left around 5:00 PM. (28th Central News Agency)
