Male Corpse Found Floating in Binjiang Park 131

A blue thread long gown and a straw hat were found at the beach of Binjiang Park in Wusong a few days ago. It was unknown who had lost them there, and it caused some suspicion. Unexpectedly, at dawn yesterday, a male corpse was found floating on the beach. He was about forty years old, wearing a striped pongee short shirt and Xiangyun gauze trousers. No family members have come forward to identify him. The long gown left on the beach is presumed to belong to the deceased. Yesterday, Zhou Lansheng, the local headman, reported the case to the local court for an investigation. In the afternoon, Prosecutor Ouyang Shu, accompanied by Investigator Shen Qixiu, was commissioned to conduct the investigation.

Fire at Zhaojia Road 132

At 7:40 PM last night, a fire broke out on the mezzanine of No. 672 Zhaojia Road, inside the city, which is a paper-made mourning object shop called the First Ling, owned by Gong Wangchun from Suzhou. The shop employees discovered the fire, but it was too late to extinguish it. In addition, paper-made objects are easily flammable. The police officer on duty immediately reported the fire to the Fire Brigade and the Old North Gate Police Station by telephone. Fire trucks from various districts arrived at the scene and made every effort to extinguish the fire. Chief Shen Zhenhua supervised and directed the firefighters to fight the fire. It took about an hour to extinguish the fire, which spread to the upper floors of No. 674 and No. 676 on either side, destroying a total of three buildings. Gong Guichun, the person in charge of the shop, was taken to the police station. According to his statement, he was outside and did not know the cause of the fire, and he had no insurance. He was handed over to the court for further investigation.

Sports News

China Team to Depart South Soon, Rong Qizhao is the Leader, Nineteen Team Members in Total, Yu Hengzhi Publishes Report of Coordination With Java 143

The Shanghai China Football Team will depart this afternoon at 3:00 PM on the French postal ship Armis to Java. There are nineteen members of the team, led by Rong Qizhao. Yu Hengzhi, the team's manager, published an article on the team's organization, for the public to know the truth.

Full Team List

(Leader) Rong Qizhao (Manager) Yu Hengzhi (Team Members) Xu Ting, Li Ning, Jiang Shanjing, Guan Xun'an, Liang Shutang, Xu Jingcheng, Chen Zhenxiang, Jiang Lu, Sun Jinshun, Li Yichen, Chen Jiaqiu, Jin Yongsen, Zheng Jiliang, Cao Guicheng, Mai Su, Li Guozhao, He Jiaqiang

Announcement of Process

Since winning both the International Cup of the Nations Football Tournament and the Sino-Portuguese International Cup, the Shanghai China Football Team has become famous overseas. People from all regions of the South Seas Islands have repeatedly expressed their admiration for the high skills of domestic teams in competitions and their remarkable achievements. The Java Qunli Sports Association sent a letter to the National Sports Federation of China inviting the Shanghai China Team to compete there during the summer vacation, to broaden the horizons of overseas Chinese and to learn from others. All travel expenses and accommodation are to be borne by the Association. The Federation, considering the upcoming National Games and the World Games in Germany next year, intended to train talents. These opportunities were highly desirable, not only for the individual achievements of the players but also for the cultivation of talents in Shanghai and the country. The intention was good, and the effect was grand. Why not do it? The Federation immediately accepted and commissioned the China Football Committee to carefully discuss and prepare the team. I, Yu, was commissioned to be the manager, and I contacted the team members of the China Team. Everyone expressed their sympathy and was ready to go. They trained in Shen Garden at 6:00 AM every day to gather strength so that they would not disappoint the enthusiasm of the overseas Chinese. However, due to the professional relationships of each person, it was necessary to formally request leave from their respective institutions in both the public and private sectors. After a month, the good things were difficult to achieve. Some players could not travel as they wished. The reason was that some people held the view of promoting football, but they only had a limited view. The purpose of sports is to increase the health of the people and is closely related to the strength of the country. Sitting in a well and watching the sky is definitely not the perspective that should be had when promoting sports. There are many talented people in the team, and it is not possible to stop the southern expedition because of the absence of a few players. The other party hopes for a strong Chinese team, and we are afraid of disappointing the enthusiasm of the people there. Therefore, we had no choice but to invite players from Hong Kong to make up for the shortfall. The main purpose of this trip is to train talents. Whether it is Hong Kong or Shanghai, they belong to the same country. This strategy cannot be said to be wrong. It is regrettable that I, who is committed to promotion, am willing to tie and untie the bell, which is contrary to my original intention. Before leaving, I would like to inform you of the process and hope that all sectors of society will understand the imperfections of the handling. (Yu Hengzhi)

Very Strong Strength

There are seventeen members of the team, plus the leader and manager, for a total of nineteen people. The players were originally selected from Shanghai, but Zhang Yecai, Chen Hongguang, Feng Yunyou, Gu Shangquan, Jia Youliang and others were unable to travel due to other engagements. Therefore, they had no choice but to invite Mai Su, Li Guozhao, Cao Zhucheng, He Jiacheng, and Zheng Jiliang, who had already gone to Singapore, to join the team (twelve people from Shanghai). It is planned to have a total of fifteen games in Java. The number of matches that will be arranged when visiting other locations is not included. It is expected to return home in early September. The team's forward power is the strongest, and the mid-line is weaker, but Li Guozhao's ball skills have reached the upper level and can still cope. The defense is similar to the mid-line. However, it is said that Mai Su's skills are second to none in Hong Kong, and he is even better than Li Tiansheng. Unfortunately, there is only one goalkeeper, Xu Heng. If there are no special circumstances, he should be able to complete the task happily. In short, the team's strength is sufficient, and it is expected that this trip will have satisfactory results.

First Preparatory Committee Meeting for Shanghai Preliminary for National Games Decides on Classified Selections and Emphasis on Training, No Centralized Preliminary Meeting, but Strive for Sufficient Training, Various Selection Committees Also Held Group Meetings Yesterday 144

The Preparatory Committee for the Shanghai Preliminary of the Sixth National Games held its first meeting at Yipinxiang yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM. The details are recorded as follows:

Attending Committee Members

Including Director Pan, Shen Siliang, Jiang Jianbai, Shao Rugan, Rong Qizhao, Wang Fudan, Ling Xitao, Jiang Xiangqing, Ma Chonggan, Chen Gongtai, Chen Yongcheng, Yu Hengzhi, Zhang Zizhen, Zhou Jiaqi, Shi Zhiqian, Qu Yue, Wang Zhuangfei, Wang Keyong, Hu Zongfan, Shen Kunnan, Lu Lihua, Yu Ziyu, Zhang Yuansheng, Le Xiule, Jiang Lianggui, Lu Zhongen, Zhou Junren, Chen Bingde, Li Feiyun, Peng Sanmei, Chen Xuliang, Tong Zhongyi, Liu Desheng, Zhu Lianxiang, Luo Shuqing, Chen Weiming, Ye Dami, and other thirty people.

Chairman's Report

Chairman Pan reported that today is the first meeting of the Preparatory Committee for the Shanghai Preliminary of the Sixth National Games. Now, as the date of the National Games is approaching and the summer vacation is near, how should our city's representatives to the National Games be selected, and what should be the training arrangements after the selection? Detailed discussions should be held. Shen Siliang also put forward his opinions, advocating that a large-scale sports meeting should not be held to save expenses, and put forward several methods for joint discussion and publication of opinions.

Decision Principles

The principle was immediately decided. This year, the method of item-by-item selection will be adopted, and no centralized preliminary meeting will be held. The selection methods, training methods, locations, dates, and expenses for each sport will be decided by the respective selection committees, and then reported to the Education Bureau for review. Then, the various selection committees will hold group meetings, followed by a gathering for dinner.

Track and Field Training

Regarding the issue of sending track and field athletes to Qingdao for summer training, it was decided that the Municipal Education Bureau would formally send Dong Shuzhao, Jia Lianren, Wang Zhenglin, Wang He, Zhang Jiakui, Gong Wanyu, Chen Jiayou, and Sun Huibei to Qingdao for training. In addition, a summer training camp for male and female track and field athletes will be set up in Shanghai. All athletes who participated in the International Games this year, except for the eight selected to go to Qingdao for training, are expected to stay in Shanghai for training during the summer vacation. The list of six people sent by the Municipal Education Bureau that was reported yesterday is not accurate. The above-mentioned eight selected people must bring their two-inch photos to the Municipal Central District Education Bureau for registration next Monday (July 1).

Track and Field All-Around

According to Shen Siliang's written opinion on the preliminary competition, individual preliminary competitions will be held for each sport. For male and female track and field and all-around events, the top ten outstanding athletes of both genders will be selected based on their usual results and sent to the Qingdao summer training class for training. Another training class will be organized in Shanghai to train the second-tier players as a group. If necessary, another preliminary competition will be held after the summer vacation to supplement the team, so as to avoid any regret.

Football and Baseball

There will be no preliminary competition for the baseball team. The current players from various universities and the China Baseball Team composed of various sectors will be the official representatives to attend the National Games in the future. The team has already participated in the Shanghai Baseball League, which is the best training opportunity. The football team will be based on the twelve Shanghai players from the China Team that are currently on the expedition to Java. In the future, outstanding players who were unable to participate in the expedition due to other matters will be selected to join the team. Therefore, this expedition to the south by the Shanghai China Team is also an excellent preparation for the Shanghai team to attend the National Games.

Volleyball, Basketball, and Volleyball

There will be no separate preliminary competition for men's tennis. The selection committee will observe the level of each person's competition this season and select them. There are many talents in volleyball. In order to establish contact, the selection committee stated that it plans to select the elite of Shanghai to form two teams and train them diligently. Then, a team will be selected from these two teams. The situation in basketball is more difficult and complicated, and preliminary competitions will be necessary. Or, the same method as volleyball can be used, first selecting excellent players to organize two or several teams, and then making further selections.

Men's and Women's Swimming

It is also planned not to hold a preliminary competition. The selection committee will pay attention to the individual results of each person this season and make a preliminary selection. If necessary, a second preliminary selection will be made to supplement the team.

Women's Ball Games

Preliminary competitions must be held for women's basketball, volleyball, softball, and tennis. First, the selection committees will pay attention to the talents of each school, and then hold a preliminary competition in early September. In short, it is estimated that individual preliminary competitions will be used and all efforts will be used for training.

Jiangsu Education Fund Allocation Method: 300,000+ Yuan Allocated This Term 153

The monthly education fund allocation for Jiangsu Province is approximately 245,000 yuan. Traditionally, rural normal schools and provincial primary schools receive their allocations half a month earlier, and secondary schools receive them one month earlier than normal schools, vocational schools, and social education institutions. (For example, currently, rural normal schools and provincial primary schools have received allocations up to the first half of June, normal schools, vocational schools, and social education institutions have received allocations up to the second half of May, and secondary schools have received allocations up to the first half of May.) It is reported that the Jiangsu Education Fund Auditing Committee held a meeting on the 25th of this month and has decided on a unified allocation method for the future. This means that the allocation notices issued to all schools and institutions this time will be filled out up to the first half of June for secondary schools. The remaining half of June will be deducted from each secondary school's administrative income to serve as the funding for the second half of June (with adjustments made for surpluses or deficits). For rural normal schools, primary schools, normal schools, vocational schools, and even social education institutions, the allocation notices will all be filled out up to the second half of June. It is also reported that the Jiangsu Education Fund Office is re-issuing the allocation notices (usually filled out for half a month, but now, due to the unified allocation up to the second half of June, additional notices must be filled out). They are requesting that the auditors sign each one and that the Education Department affix its seal. At the same time, personnel are being dispatched to urge each county to submit their education funds. It is estimated that there are over 200,000 yuan in the treasury, but even with the funds remitted by the counties on the 27th, there is still a shortfall of about 100,000 yuan. However, due to the good harvest this season, the counties should be able to remit the remaining 100,000 yuan within the next ten days. To facilitate the allocation of funds to the schools, distributions will begin sequentially after the beginning of July. From July onwards, all schools and institutions will receive their funding in the same month, eliminating the previous discrepancies.

Leave Application Procedures for Primary School Teachers and Staff Attending Summer School: Municipal Education Bureau Orders All Schools to Comply 158

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued an order to all municipal and private registered primary schools in this city stating that, upon investigation, many students of this year's summer school for primary school teachers and staff and students of the summer training course for private registered primary school teachers and staff who are serving as heads or deputy heads of sub-groups in the literacy education service corps have applied for leave. A unified approach should be established and ordered to be followed. The order cites Article 7 of the "Guidelines for Sub-Group Work" issued by the Literacy Education Service Corps: "Although there is a summer vacation in July, at least one of the head or deputy head of each sub-group should remain at the school for one or two days each week to provide teaching guidance to the members and training or testing for the public taught by the members of each group." The regulations stipulate that the organization of this service sub-group is based on the school as a unit, that is, each school establishes a sub-group, with the principal as the head and the head teacher as the deputy head. Based on this, it is sufficient for each school to have one person remain at the school for one or two days each week during the summer vacation in July to handle the work of the sub-group. The Bureau now stipulates that each school may allow one head of the sub-group to take leave to return to school to handle the work of the sub-group on Saturdays and Sundays each week during the summer school period. For the rest of the time, they must still attend school as usual. Students serving as deputy heads of the sub-group may not apply for leave separately, so that both the promotion of literacy education and the teacher's own professional development can be taken into account. All schools are ordered to comply with this order, and no disregard is allowed. For schools that have previously submitted special requests for instructions, no further orders will be issued after this general order. Please also be informed. This order.

Publishing World

A Self-Rescue Plan for the Publishing Industry 163

— Fan Zhongyun

—Unified Sales Organization—

Currently, the most pressing difficulties for China's publishing industry are: (1) competition among publishers, (2) manipulation by middlemen, (3) difficulty in recovering payments, and (4) challenges in book promotion. I believe that sluggish business and difficulty in capital turnover are secondary, as resolving the former issues would naturally eliminate the latter difficulties.

To solve these four difficulties, publishers must have a fundamental realization: from now on, focus solely on publishing and refrain from engaging in sales. I believe this realization is especially necessary for publishers with small capital. Publishers with large capital can engage in planned production on one hand and establish sales outlets in various locations to distribute books nationwide on the other hand. However, small-capital publishers lack the strength to do so. Conversely, they face oppression from large publishers on one hand and internal strife among peers on the other. Therefore, to resist the oppression of large publishers and seek self-reliance, small publishers today must unite and separate publishing from sales, making them independent operations. Based on this principle of division of labor between production and distribution, I propose that publishers jointly establish a unified sales organization. The reasons and methods are as follows:

Currently, small bookstores must each set up a retail sales department to sell their complete range of books, and these stores must be located on Fuzhou Road, where land prices are very high. The Fuzhou Road area is originally a commercial center. The reason why small bookstores must gather here is partly because large bookstores such as Commercial Press and China Bookstore are located there, and partly because Shanghai lacks a central cultural area, as so-called scholars are scattered in the east, west, north, and south suburbs, not concentrated in one place. Therefore, it is indeed very uneconomical for small bookstores to independently open retail stores on Fuzhou Road. If they can cooperate and establish a general sales organization, it will definitely provide many benefits to each bookstore's finances. Moreover, it is clear that small stores cannot compete with large department stores. Therefore, the establishment of a unified sales organization will inevitably attract more attention from buyers than individual small bookstores. This is the economic saving for publishers, the first benefit.

Secondly, with a unified sales organization, the malpractices of exploitation and manipulation by middlemen, as well as unpaid debts, can be completely eliminated. The most helpless situation for small bookstores in Shanghai is that they have to entrust the sales in various places to general booksellers. Because of the exploitation of these booksellers, Shanghai publishers have to set high prices for their books, but their income is still only 70% or 80% of the price, and even recovering the capital is not easy. However, readers who buy books must pay the full price or even add postage. Therefore, the existence of middlemen is detrimental to publishers and only increases the suffering of readers due to high prices. It is indeed an obstacle to the future development of culture. If there is a unified sales organization with a head office in Shanghai and branch offices in various places, these middlemen will not only have no chance to profit, but also the malpractice of unpaid debts like today can be completely eliminated. Because today's booksellers often take advantage of the independent operations of small bookstores and simply ignore the payments to Bookstore A. Bookstore A, because it is far away in another city, is inconvenient to collect the debt and has to suffer the loss, deciding not to wholesale books to them anymore. Bookstore A believes that this will put the bookseller in dire straits, but the reality is not so. They can still get books from Bookstore A through their dealings with Bookstore B. Therefore, unless bookstores A, B, C, and D can unite, booksellers who owe money in other cities can still find ways to wholesale books from various bookstores. There are really many such things, which is what small bookstores feel most painful about. If a unified sales organization can be established, booksellers in other cities who want to wholesale publications from bookstores A, B, C, and D must go through this organization, then they will have no way to use their cunning skills. Moreover, with the existence of branch organizations in various places, they can directly collect debts, and they will have no room to arbitrarily delay payments. This is the operational convenience that a unified sales organization gives to publishers, the second benefit.

Furthermore, with a unified general sales organization in Shanghai and branch organizations in the interior, books can be immediately distributed to the whole country after publication to reach readers, unlike today, where publishers struggle to find readers, and readers, although seeing advertisements, struggle to find bookstores to buy books, or suffer losses from being deceived by advertisements after painstakingly remitting money and buying books with poor content. This phenomenon of separation between the publishing industry and the reading community can be connected with a unified sales organization, and it can also avoid the oppression of large publishers. The advantage of large publishers is that they have strong capital, so they can set up branches everywhere, while small publishers cannot. Now, if there is a unified sales organization, small publishers will have the same benefits as large publishers and will not have to worry about the monopoly oppression of large publishers. This is the third benefit.

Also, if the sales organization is separated from the publishing organization and operated independently, publishers can focus on publishing without having to worry about sales. In terms of organization, all that is needed is an editorial department to handle everything properly. (Printing, etc., can be handled by specialized printing organizations.) In this way, not only can capital be concentrated, which is economically beneficial, but also the concentration of manpower can achieve specialized results in operation. This division of labor between production and distribution is the most advanced point of modern capitalist production. Since the publishing industry is a modern industry, it must adopt advanced methods, otherwise, it will inevitably lag behind and be eliminated. This is the fourth benefit.

As for how to successfully establish this unified sales organization, I believe that it must first have huge capital, at least three to four hundred thousand, to establish sales organizations all over the country. Otherwise, the sales network will not be widespread, which will greatly affect the promotion of books. Secondly, the organization of this organization must be a third party unrelated to the publishing industry to maintain a neutral position, but at the same time, it also needs the participation of publishers to maintain contact and ensure that publishers participating in the organization immediately abandon their sales operations.

I believe that the publishing industry is the most promising among all industries in our country. With the popularization of education and the progress of culture, the number of literate people will inevitably increase, and the business market will only continue to expand. Moreover, because the publishing industry is a cultural undertaking, it enjoys special benefits such as postage and tariffs compared to other commercial businesses. This is a convenience that no other business has. Furthermore, almost no industry in our country today can escape the oppression of imperialists. Industries such as tobacco, cotton yarn, and flour are all in a difficult situation due to the dumping of foreign goods and the competition of foreign factories. Only the publishing industry does not have this phenomenon. In China, it is simply a monopoly world. Therefore, if it can be managed properly, there is much room for development. The current economic downturn is only a temporary phenomenon. If we can strive for reform, there is definitely a solution.

Impressions of Various Bookstores (Continued) 164

— Li Hengzhi

19. The Masses Bookstore

This bookstore has a relatively long history and is quite tenacious. Although it is in its twilight years, it is not afraid of long journeys and is running alongside others.

Those who pay attention to the book industry will think of "running after others" when mentioning the Masses Bookstore. In the early days, some of the Masses' "anti-imperialist" books did indeed gain considerable profits, but most of them were pieced together and could not withstand the competition of later emerging publishers. Soon, with the development of new literature, the Masses also published many literary books, and these literary books were not far from the "worship of ×," and now there is no foothold. Later, there came some compilations such as "×× Selections," which can be said to be more meaningful among the publications of the Masses.

The Masses' storefront is only this small half-room between the Modern Era (formerly New Moon) and others. Because it is sandwiched between the beautiful storefronts of other stores, the Masses' storefront looks even smaller. However, the Masses' storefront does not lose its customers because of its small size, but most of its customers are not its own. Previously, because the storefront of "Dawn" was attached to the Masses, it brought a lot of immediate sales to the Masses. Later, because the Shanghai Magazine Company was established in the Masses, it even reached the point of "bustling with activity." However, since "Dawn" and "Shanghai" established their own storefronts one after another, the Masses' business was naturally hit. However, the Masses has always been confident in "running after others." It then changed to a "magazine company" itself and also published several pictorials and other periodicals. However, following others is mostly "lagging behind." Moreover, the publications it publishes, whether in content or form, are equally poor. If there is anything noteworthy about the Masses, it is only the previous "Sound of the Tide" and the current "Mangzhong."

20. The Guangyi Bookstore

The Guangyi Bookstore mainly sells old books, but it has also published a few new books. It is said that Guangyi's business in old books (ancient books) is very considerable every year. The nature of the old books it publishes will not be discussed today, but in terms of new books, it is indeed too speculative. Looking at the things it publishes, such as "××× Methods," the form is indeed very fashionable, but the content itself still needs to study the "methods" to a large extent. Originally, it is impossible to produce anything other than crude and shoddy articles with a manuscript fee of one yuan or a few cents per thousand words.

The Guangyi's new book publication seems to be decreasing now (or even non-existent). We cannot say that this is not a "good" strategy for Guangyi.

21. Guangming, Lehua, and Wenyi

This joint storefront on Fourth Avenue has attracted the attention of readers before, because when the books of various bookstores were still sold at the actual price, the three storefronts marked out the "woodblock print 30% off, foreign edition 20% off" long-term discount method. Naturally, many readers ran to their place. However, soon, each store with a storefront on Fourth Avenue, due to the impact on business, stopped issuing books one after another. At the same time, "new books at half price" also became a common trend.

These three bookstores can be said to be the typical "family bookstores." They do it on a small scale, and there is little division of labor in editing and business. They watch the opportunity, and when they see an opportunity, they publish one or two books that adapt to the opportunity. Sometimes, they hit the bullseye, such as the League of Nations Investigation Team Report and Mussolini's Autobiography. The business is not bad. However, ultimately, they cannot be said to be publishers, but rather sellers. (To be continued)

Various Methods of a Writer's Swindling 165

— Zushun

Zhang Kebiao once wrote The Art of Literary Advancement, revealing the secrets of fame, but Mr. Zhang finally failed to the point of seeking a job through classified ads, which shows that everyone can do tricks, but each has different skills. If you don't use it properly, you still can't succeed. Now I will introduce a few small tricks that are easier to play than the big ones.

1. Kill Two Birds with One Stone A writer who has not yet become famous has worked hard to write or translate a book and of course wants to sell it to a bookstore for publication. However, 99% of the time, you will not find a buyer, so you have to apply this method: please have a famous person lead the way, put your name behind his, and this way, he will find a place to publish for you. If it succeeds, you can give him half of the manuscript fee. And of course you shouldn't feel distressed, thinking that you only get half of the reward, because without him, you will never! never get even this half.

2. Kick Away the Ladder If you read a book and there are chapters quoted from some famous rare books, you should keep them in mind and find a way to quote them whenever you have the opportunity, but never state that you are quoting from that book, because that would be too uneconomical. You have to just note the name of the original book, and the chapter and page numbers must be stated clearly. If that book is in Italian, Latin, or Indian, be sure to copy the original text word for word, whether you understand it or not. This method not only shows that you are knowledgeable and talented, but also makes readers respect you as an honest writer.

Translating works from English or Japanese to Russian or Italian without noting the translation can also be considered a type of this method.

3. Avoid the Important and Dwell on the Trivial This third type of swindling is similar to the second type, but it is limited to foreign languages. Many famous works cannot be read because they are too long or because the original is not easy to find. Fortunately, there are many magazines abroad that specialize in doing summaries and detailed reviews and introductions. If you subscribe to a few copies every month, it is like reading the original text. When you are happy, you can translate a few paragraphs, just don't state whether it is translated or written by yourself, or vaguely note the words "excerpted translation" so that people don't understand whether you are excerpting from the original text or from the excerpt. The beauty of this method is that you can gradually build an image of erudition in the hearts of pure readers, and mischievous people cannot find your handle.

4. Grafting One Branch to Another When you see someone else's article with detailed citations and novel philosophy, and you are moved by it, you can apply this method. You can write an article close to this topic and quote all the citations and textual research one by one. This way, you can also list fifty or sixty notes and reference books at the end of your work. Who can not admire your extensive knowledge, and who can know that you only read a short article? Moreover, this method is absolutely not dangerous. Even if it is discovered, they can only sneer for a while and can never convict you of plagiarism.

5. Turning Guest into Host Dr. Hu Shih said that he can only get three or four hundred words per hour for translation work, which shows that this work is really not easy to do. It is really a thankless job. On the one hand, no matter how well you do it, there is always room for people to criticize. On the other hand, after spending so much effort, you only acted as an introducer. People always say that Wells' The Outline of History is good, but they won't say that the world history outline translated by so-and-so is really good. In this way, hard and difficult things, sometimes encountering a word or sentence that you have no way to deal with, you have to shake your head and think about it when eating and walking, but in the end you get a few yuan per thousand words and there is no follow-up, how pitiful. But it is really not easy to write a book by yourself, so it is better to change the translation to compilation, find a few books and piece them together, extracting a section here and half a chapter there. If you can't translate it, just don't, isn't that refreshing? If you are timid, you can note this sentence in the preface or postscript: "This book is mostly based on the ×× book by ××," and there is no danger at all. Recently, a gentleman translated a Japanese-published engineering manual, and even the printing errors are exactly the same, but in the preface, he said that this type of book is the first one compiled by Chinese people. His courage really makes us admire him.

Of course, there are many ways to swindle, but as long as the people who apply the above methods are black-hearted and thick-skinned, there is absolutely no danger. If readers cannot understand, I can still provide various examples for you to refer to.

All-Metal Vacuum Tube 166

— Xingshi

Although there are many styles of vacuum tubes on the market now, their shells are all made of glass. Anyone who has played with radios knows that in many devices, a metal shielding cover must be added to the outside of the vacuum tube to obtain excellent performance. This not only costs money, but also increases the size of the radio a lot. But now, that's good. The United States has invented an all-metal vacuum tube. This invention is bound to open up a new path for future vacuum tube manufacturing.

This vacuum tube is made entirely of metal except for the glass beads used for insulation where the lead wires come out. Its volume is much smaller than the current glass-shelled tubes, and it is undoubtedly more sturdy. Because metal shells are easy to manufacture, the cost can also be reduced. This type of vacuum tube is easy to dissipate heat and has excellent shielding performance. It will soon be able to replace the position of today's vacuum tube.

The metal shell of this new tube is cylindrical, with a slightly smaller diameter at the top. The grid of the high-frequency tube is also at the top. The wires drawn from each electrode first pass through a small glass ball and are heated and melted. Small holes are drilled in the metal shell where the lead wires pass through. A new alloy (a combination of iron, nickel, and cobalt) called Fernico is placed around the holes. Its coefficient of expansion is exactly the same as glass. This is very important and can be said to be a major reason for the success of this vacuum tube. The glass beads are placed at the openings of the holes and melted together. Because of that alloy, the glass beads and the metal shell can be firmly bonded together and will not break due to heat.

The lead wires inside the vacuum tube are short and straight, so they are more suitable for short waves. Its volume is also reduced as a result. Moreover, because of the convenience of manufacturing the metal shell, it can be very close to the internal electrodes, greatly reducing the internal screen-grid capacitance to about one-third of that of the current vacuum tube, so the amplification factor of the vacuum tube can be increased without causing instability.

The metal shell itself is connected to the ground wire, so the trouble of adding a shielding cover can be completely avoided. The number of pins on the vacuum tube is also one more than similar tubes because the metal shell is grounded.

There are now ten types of this all-metal vacuum tube, six of which are being mass-produced by the Alsea Company. One is a double-diode twin-tube, with the cathodes of the two diodes separated and isolated in the middle, but its height is only eight-fifths of an inch, which is much smaller than the current vacuum tube.

Automatic Noise Suppression 167

— Mingxiang

Generally, the more vacuum tubes a radio has and the higher its sensitivity, the stronger the radio's noise will be. The source of this noise is sometimes not due to disturbances from atmospheric static electricity and man-made static electricity, nor is it caused by damaged parts inside the radio. For example, the impact and movement of electrons on the wires, as well as the emission of electrons in the vacuum tube, are the main causes of this unavoidable noise. When the radio is turned on, before the music has been tuned in, hissing noise fills the ears, which is really unpleasant. Fortunately, the advancement of radio technology is constantly making satisfactory solutions to difficult problems. The automatic noise suppression described in this article is also one of the latest successes.

The main component that completes the automatic noise suppression function is still the vacuum tube, the heart of the radio. The basic principle is to use the rectification effect of the detector tube to generate a control voltage that is supplied to another specially designed control vacuum tube. The effect of this control tube is to completely stop the audio frequency amplification section of the radio from working when it has not been tuned to the signal voltage input. If an external signal carrier arrives, the control tube immediately and automatically restores the audio frequency stage to its original task and broadcasts beautiful programs. Therefore, automatic noise suppression devices and automatic volume control are essential conditions for high-end radios. This control tube is usually specifically referred to as the Noise Suppression Control Tube, and some are simply called Q tubes.

The diagram shows the simplest automatic noise suppression circuit. V1 is a diode used as a detector using the rectification principle; V2 is a triode used for automatic noise suppression; V3 is the controlled audio frequency amplifier tube.

When the input transformer is not receiving an external signal, V1 has no screen current flowing, that is, no negative voltage is supplied to the V2 grid, so the screen current passing through R2 is the largest. This extremely large screen current causes V3 to generate an extremely high negative voltage to supply to the V3 grid, sufficient to cut off the V1 screen current and completely lose its amplification effect. At this time, the audio frequency stage of the radio has been suppressed and cannot work. If a signal is input, V2 generates a screen current. At both ends of R, there are DC and audio frequency voltages. This DC voltage can be supplied to V2 to increase its grid negative potential, causing the screen current to cut off. There is no voltage drop on R2. At this time, the audio frequency signal voltage on R is fed to the V3 grid through C4. Because the V3 grid negative voltage is extremely low, it can already fulfill its amplification duties.

The working principles of automatic noise suppression and automatic volume control are the same, that is, changing the grid voltage of the amplifier tube. However, the difference is that the former belongs to the audio frequency stage, and the latter belongs to the high-frequency or intermediate frequency stage.

Methods for Preventing Howling in Low-Frequency Amplification 168

— Weng Yanhuo

Howling in low-frequency amplification is caused by low-frequency oscillation generated from the amplifier. Because the iron core coil of the transformer contains a considerable amount of distributed capacitance and self-inductance, it forms an oscillation circuit, which is oscillated by the magnetic-electric effect of the wiring and the static-electric effect. Although the initial sound of the oscillation is very small, it becomes an ear-piercing howl after amplification. Here is a brief description of the prevention methods:

(1) The grid circuit should be firmly connected, short, and the shorter the better.

(2) It is not easy to oscillate when using resistance amplification.

(3) The position must be arranged properly.

(4) If transformer amplification is used, the transformers should be separated so that the iron cores are at right angles to each other. Even better, isolate them with a metal cover.

(5) A fixed capacitor of 0.001-0.002 microfarads can be installed between the grid circuit and the filament of the second-stage amplification.

(6) Any wiring should be short.

Method for Self-Made Carbon Resistor Ohm Disc Identification 170

— Chen Binhui

Currently, there is a rotating disc on the market for identifying the ohm value of carbon resistors, priced at about forty or fifty cents. However, it seems to be a shoddy product, so the author went home and made one himself based on its appearance. It is very convenient and accurate to use, and the manufacturing method is very simple. Why not make one yourself for emergencies and to prevent money from flowing out? Now, the detailed manufacturing process is listed below:

Materials: One square piece of cardboard (or thicker white paper)

Seven colors of paint (or colored paper cutouts can also be used)

A small amount of No. 24 enameled wire

First, cut the cardboard as shown in Figure 1, fold it along the dotted line, and cut three fan-shaped holes as shown in the figure. Then, cut three circular cardboard pieces, A, B, and C, as shown in Figure 2. Divide them into several grids as shown in the figure, and mark the ohm numbers. Dye them in various colors. Everything is clearly marked in the figures, so there is no need to repeat it.

Finally, use enameled wire to fix it as shown in the figure so that it can rotate. Thus, a simple and practical resistor identification disc is completed, as shown in Figure 3.

For example, if there is a resistor with a brown body, a black head, and an orange center, we rotate the grid above the "body" character to brown, the grid on the "head" character to black, and the grid on the "center" character to orange. As shown in the figure, we can know that this resistor is 10,000 ohms.

Homemade Soldering Flux 171

— He Feng

When wiring a radio receiver, soldering is unavoidable. There are usually two types of soldering: one using rosin and the other using zinc chloride (commonly known as muriatic acid). It is easy to work with zinc chloride, but it requires more skill to use rosin. However, many amateurs agree that using zinc chloride for soldering has more disadvantages than advantages, because when the zinc chloride is heated by the soldering iron, it explodes with a bang, scattering powder in all directions, easily corroding the equipment. If it is not cleaned thoroughly, it will turn green over time due to chemical changes, and even gradually corrode the soldered area, hindering the radio's operation. There is no such drawback with rosin soldering. However, rosin is more difficult to use. Now, based on amateur experience, the rosin is crushed into powder, placed in "Vaseline" (available at pharmacies), and mixed evenly. Steam it slightly over water for a moment, and then use it. It is very convenient, and its performance is no different from all the soldering fluxes sold on the market. If you have time, you might as well try it.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits 179

—(Wan Gong)

"People rarely know the faults of their own children, and rarely know the vigor of their own seedlings." These are the words of Confucius. Zhu Xi added two annotations to it: "Those who are indulgent are not clear, and those who are greedy are insatiable." Later generations extended its meaning and evolved it into two common sayings: "A son is always one's own good, and a woman is always someone else's good." Although the examples are different, the meaning is the same. I think it is not entirely true; beauty is in the eye of the beholder, and everyone who has a love history will admit this, right? Isn't this "a woman is always one's own good"? Seeing other people's children become successful, promoted and wealthy, who doesn't envy them and hate their own children for not living up to expectations? Isn't this "a son is always someone else's good"? Looking at these two examples, not only is the common saying upside down, but even the words of Confucius are a bit "mixed up". Zhu Jia's words are more glib.

Occasional Notes on Reading 180

—Cat Hermit Master

Among Kunqu operas, there is a play called "Fifteen Strings of Cash," which describes the story of Prefect Kuang reversing a wrongful conviction. There is also "The Legend of Fifteen Strings of Cash," which was written by Zhu Suchen of Wu County in the Qing Dynasty, and is similar to the Kunqu opera. Prefect Kuang was an honest and upright official, and was known as "Kuang Qingtian" (meaning Kuang, the clear sky). Since he was a famous official of the Ming Dynasty, the story of "Fifteen Strings of Cash" should have originated in the Ming Dynasty. However, things are not always the case. The actual story of "Fifteen Strings of Cash" originated in the Song Dynasty in Nanjing. Recently, I read a passage in Qu Yuan's "Random Notes from the Chunzai Hall":

In Lin'an, Southern Song Dynasty, there was a man named Liu Gui, courtesy name Junjian, who had a wife named Wang and a concubine named Chen. One day, he took his wife to celebrate the birthday of his father-in-law. His father-in-law, Wang Weng, gave him fifteen strings of cash because he was poor, so that he could earn a living. He kept his daughter but let his son-in-law return first. On the way, he met his friend, drank with him, and got drunk. When he returned home, his concubine saw the money he was carrying and asked why. Liu Gui, drunk, teased her and said: Because my family is poor and cannot live together, I have rented you to someone. This is the rental money. I will send you there tomorrow. After speaking, he went to bed and fell asleep. The concubine thought of telling her parents, so she went to the home of her neighbor, Zhu Sanlao, told him the reason, and stayed overnight. She left at dawn. Liu Gui was still fast asleep and had not woken up. A thief broke into his house, stole his money. Liu woke up in surprise, got up and chased him. He happened to find an ax on the ground. The thief took the ax and killed Liu, taking all the money. The next day, the neighbors saw that his door had not been opened for a long time, and when they went inside, they found the situation. Zhu Sanlao then said that his concubine had stayed overnight with him. So they searched together. The concubine, halfway on the road, rested because she was tired. A man named Cui Ning, who sold silk in the city, also earned fifteen strings of cash. He rested with her. The pursuers arrived and wanted to take them both back. When the officer heard, he said that Cui and the concubine had an affair, killed her husband, stole his money, and were fleeing together. They were publicly executed in the market. Later, his wife, because her husband died and her family was poor, her father, Wang Weng, sent someone to welcome her home. On the way, she encountered heavy rain and took refuge in a forest. She was captured by a robber and taken as his wife. She accidentally mentioned the events of several years ago, and the wife knew that the robber was the one who killed her husband. She took the opportunity to report to the Lin'an government, and the truth came to light.

According to this, the Kunqu opera "Fifteen Strings of Cash" is very similar, probably because later generations wanted to praise Kuang Qingtian for his honesty, so they developed this story.

In the Waiting Room 181

—Ba Ling

About the second Tuesday last week? I was involved in a friend's case, and I started questioning. On the one hand, I wanted to attend the hearing; at the same time, I wanted to add some experience to me, this novice, so I drove straight to the Nanshi District Court. After arriving at the court, because it was still early, I waited in the court's waiting room for more than an hour.

The waiting room, what a terrible and sacred, solemn place it is? What's more, it's the waiting room of the court, which makes people feel a different kind of mood.

When I was waiting in the waiting room, there were already many people waiting to be tried, and many more were arriving one after another? If we take the gender of men and women to count, then men accounted for eight tenths, and women only accounted for two tenths.

I sat in the waiting room, carefully observing the people who were about to be tried. Some were frowning, as if a huge disaster was coming upon them; some were whispering, discussing how to deal with the judge's questions? Some were thinking silently, as if repenting of their mistakes. What especially aroused my infinite emotion was that the defendant and the plaintiff were in the same room. On the surface, they still shook hands and said hello when they met, but in reality, each person's mind was planning how to deal with you? Alas! This hypocritical and terrible society, here, gives people a profound hint!

In short, the court is solemn, and the waiting room is the most likely place to evoke feelings. There, I remembered what Mr. Zhu Bailu said, "Lawsuits always end in misfortune," which is really true.

—Juan Yin

Not afraid of hardship, working diligently for the public

Old Husband and Young Wife 182

—Zhou Xian

Recently, in the alley where I live, an old gentleman of sixty-three years old remarried a young girl of twenty-five years old. This event almost aroused the attention of everyone in the alley. So many busybodies were desperately probing all the news of this family as material for conversation.

This sixty-three-year-old gentleman was once the director of a tax office for a while, so he has considerable assets in his hands. Last year, his old partner died, and he felt lonely, so he married this high-achieving student from a certain girl's school through an introduction. This old gentleman's second wife is seventeen years younger than his eldest son. His youngest son is also four years older than this stepmother.

One day, at the banquet, this old gentleman, with six or seven points of drunkenness, announced his motive for marrying such a young wife: "You don't need to be surprised about my marriage. I am so old, living one day is like two and a half days. Naturally, I don't hope that someone will keep chastity for me after my death, so I married such an educated young woman. I live one day, she lives with me one day. When I kick my legs, I don't have to worry that she won't find a way out."

At the same time, his wife secretly said to her classmates: "In this way, I don't have to worry about not getting the inheritance. Isn't this stronger than demanding alimony through divorce? He is already sixty-three years old this year, and his body is not very healthy either. If I keep watch for a few years and get the inheritance, I don't have to worry about not being able to develop, right?"

The old husband has the old husband's worries, and the young wife has the young wife's ideas. Such a combination, I think, is more suitable.

Little Western Paradise 183

—Written by Zhang Henshui

Episode 15: Bitter words persuade with good intentions, no empty accusations. The sound of money and the shadows of lamps are pitiful as they sell people.

As Zhiqian spoke, Hu Xiaojiao's face slowly changed color. Finally, she twitched her nose twice, sniffing and crying. She lifted a piece of her clothes and wiped her tears, saying; "What you, sir, said is not all the truth? I have been thinking about it for two days, and I can't come up with any ideas. That Miss Yang also said that what he said was reasonable everywhere, and I was moved by what he said, so I said I would try, but I didn't say that it would definitely work." Zhiqian said: "Don't cry yet, what did he say? Maybe what he said is right, you tell me." Hu Saozi wiped away her tears, and shook her head slightly, saying: "As soon as you, sir, revealed it, I no longer believed his words. He said: The concubine will always be liked by the master. As long as the girl marries over, and acts cute in front of the master, she doesn't have to worry about the master not supporting her mother-in-law. Even if the master takes him to the south, he can often write letters, and as long as he has money, he can also take his mother and grandmother there, and he can also come back to Xi'an to see them. Soon, the train will be connected to Xi'an, and the train is very convenient. That's what he said, it sounds very nice. But I thought, I'm afraid things are not so easy. Now that Master Cheng has said it, people's hearts are made of flesh, so how can he be willing to part with her? But that Miss Yang is also too good at talking, and as soon as she speaks, I get confused." Beihai, ever since she broke that teacup, has been feeling very embarrassed, and has not spoken for a long time. Yuan then interjected: "Although I can't speak as comprehensively as Cheng Guangsheng, I also feel that you don't have to wait to sell people to make a living. You go back and discuss it, you take another route." As he spoke, his face was not turned towards Hu Saozi, as if he felt a little uneasy in his heart. (252)

Records of the Vague Fragrance 184

—Original by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Then how will this disease be diagnosed? Only the step of observing the complexion can be omitted, and the pulse can be taken directly. At that time, two small square tables had been set up on both sides of the Empress Dowager's throne, with a soft cushion spread on the table. After the four imperial physicians respectfully bowed their heads nine times, the Empress Dowager ordered two other female officials to roll up half of Yi Fu's sleeves, allowing her to sit upright on the throne in the middle, and put her arms on the small tables on both sides. Then the four imperial physicians knelt forward, all the way to the two small tables; at the same time, two female officials had already covered the Empress Dowager's arms with two very thin silk scarves, because how could such a noble person as the Empress Dowager be easily touched by irrelevant people! The four imperial physicians divided into two sides, two on each side, and carefully stretched out their hands, using their fingertips to take the Empress Dowager's pulse quietly through the silk scarf. As for taking the pulse, this method of diagnosing disease is really mysterious! They don't use a stopwatch to calculate the number of pulses, they only rely on five fingers to press, how can they know the patient's condition? I used to think it was miraculous—and I still don't understand it.

After a while, the imperial physicians on the left and right sides quietly switched places; but they never dared to peek at the Empress Dowager, although in fact they knew that there should be a procedure to look at the patient's tongue coating, or the Empress Dowager herself would not refuse, but they were always very cautious, how dare they rashly ask for the Empress Dowager's tongue? They also tried their best to avoid the Empress Dowager's gaze, and even when taking the pulse, they deliberately turned their heads a little, as if they were shy. (352)

Local Chronicles

Old Stories of the East Gate 185

—Shanghai General News Agency

In the past, when Shanghai still had a city wall, the side facing the Huangpu River was the East Gate. The Great East Gate was called Chaozong Gate, and it was located at the east end of today's Zhaojiabang Road; the Small East Gate was north of the Great East Gate, and it was called Baodai Gate, located at the east end of today's Fangbang Road. Walk past the front gate of the City God Temple and run east to reach it.

Shanghai has long been an international trading market, with foreign ships arriving in droves. At that time, of course, there were no current concession areas. The market was centered on the county seat, and merchant ships poured in from the Huangpu River, making the area outside the East Gate the focus of the dock. The Great East Gate and the Small East Gate were incredibly lively.

In the twenty-third year of the Kangxi reign of the Qing Dynasty, the sea ban was abolished. The following year, Shanghai established a customs office, called "Jianghai Great Customs," which sat outside the northeast of the Small East Gate, facing the Huangpu River; cargo ships entering the port had to pass by it, which was a strategic location.

Outside of the current Min Guo Road, connecting Taikoo Road and Zhoushan Road, there is a "Foreign Firm Street." Speaking of the history of this street, it is very long. According to the Shanghai County Chronicle compiled in the nineteenth year of the Jiaqing reign, both the county map in Volume 1 and the lane descriptions in Volume 6 have recorded this street name; from this, it can be proved that Foreign Firm Street was by no means only after the five ports were opened for trade, and the prosperity of Shanghai's foreign firms before the opening of the port can be imagined. In the Jiaqing era, Foreign Firm Street ran north from outside the Small East Gate, directly to Customs Street: and there were two parallel streets, the inner Foreign Firm Street and the outer Foreign Firm Street. Now, only one street remains.

In the twenty-third year of the Daoguang reign, Shanghai was opened as a treaty port based on the Treaty of Nanjing, and successively there were British and French settlement areas designated in the north of the city, slightly robbing the southern city of its business. The Shanghai Daotai then built another customs office at the dam outside Beidou (established in the twenty-sixth year of the Daoguang reign), called the North Customs, also known as the New Customs, and the Great Customs of the Small East Gate thus became the South Customs or Old Customs.

When the French Concession was first designated, the southern end of the east side only reached the Xinkai River, and the nature of the Xinkai River was equivalent to a "boundary creek" (Defence Creek). In the ninth month of the eleventh year of the Xianfeng reign, the French Concession was expanded for the first time. They saw the importance of the area along the river, so they repeatedly exerted pressure and obtained the expansion of the southeast of their concession, extending a tongue below the Xinkai River, all the way to the Sixteenth Wharf. At that time, the Small East Gate faced the French Concession, and Foreign Firm Street also licked that extended tongue.

After the area north of the Sixteenth Wharf outside the city was划 into the French Concession, what happened to the Old Customs? It doesn't matter, the Old Customs had already moved to the Great East Gate, because after the Customs Office of the Small East Gate was destroyed by the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom army in the tenth year of the Xianfeng reign, it was changed to working in the Rescue Bureau of the Great East Gate.

On the tongue of the French Concession, many roads were later built, using Chinese place names to name them, such as Taiwan Road, Zhoushan Road, and Fujian Road, which is very interesting. These road names are repeated with the road names in the British Concession. The Taikoo Road mentioned earlier, also written as Dagu Road, has also become one of Shanghai's repeated road names.

As the road administration of the foreign concession was improved day by day and the market became more prosperous, the Shanghai authorities felt that they had to catch up quickly. In the twenty-second year of the Guangxu reign, Shanghai County began to build a main road outside the beach of the Great East Gate, named Outer Bund; later, they built Inner Bund west of Outer Bund. As soon as the thoroughfare was built, the market naturally followed the Huangpu Bund of the British and French Concessions. Because the beach outside the Great East Gate extends into the river, the Outer Bund is not directly connected to the foreign concession, but the Inner Bund connects to the French Bund. Friends who don't often run to the East Gate, when looking for the so-called "Chinese Bund," have to ask clearly.

Shanghai Newspaper Local Supplement

Talk

Residents Should Pay Attention to Summer Cold Drinks on the Market 186

— Meng Ruo

Illness enters through the mouth; diet and health are closely related. Those who value hygiene usually pay attention to their food. Especially in summer, when various infectious diseases are prevalent, all food and drinks must be given extra attention. Once summer arrives, the hot weather makes food easily spoil. Moreover, flies are swarming, which are also vectors of cholera. Therefore, if one is careless with diet, illness is inevitable. This not only harms one's health but can also endanger one's life. As for the summer drinks sold on the market, such as iced water, sour plum juice, soda, and fruit露 (juice/syrup), many are unhygienic, and we must pay extra attention to them.

This summer, the city's health bureau is working very hard to prevent infectious diseases. Since the beginning of summer, it has been conducting city-wide immunization injections and disinfection of ditches and canals in various places. Recently, considering that the milk and cold drinks sold by various merchants in the market are consumed by many people, it is difficult to avoid the sale of inferior products mixed in without strict and constant inspections, which would harm people's health. Therefore, it specifically collected samples and ordered the health laboratory to conduct detailed inspections. Regarding milk, seven companies have been inspected this month. The number of bacteria per cubic centimeter was too high and did not meet the prescribed standards. They have been strictly ordered to pay attention to cleanliness and thoroughly disinfect. It is also heard that samples will be taken from consumers for inspection to ensure thoroughness. Regarding cold drinks, twenty-one types of soda have been inspected, and only two types passed. Forty-four types of fruit露 have been inspected, and only two types passed. Also, three samples of sour plum juice were inspected, and none passed. The unqualified products all had too many bacteria and did not meet the city's standards. If they contain germs, consumers are even more likely to get sick. The health bureau has now notified all unqualified manufacturers and ordered them to make thorough improvements for re-inspection.

From the results of this inspection by the health bureau, we find that most of the drinks sold on the market today are indeed unhygienic. The general public should pay great attention and be extra careful.

The Foot of Han Mountain 187

— Jing Fu

"The foot of Han Mountain, east of Xiang Bridge..." When such magnificent singing faintly floats into my mind, I seem to be able to distinguish that it is played from the unrestrained tone of young people! It gently awakens in me the jumping of the souls of young people, in the same mood and timbre as the song, awakening the dancing reflections of those scenes that have disappeared and become blurred like dreams...

"The foot of Han Mountain, east of Xiang Bridge..." This is a song that a group of us young people used to dance and sing often about seven or eight years ago. But now, I can only remember this

Page 18

first sentence. This can be seen as a trace of the whip of life smashing old dreams to pieces over the years! However, this mere sentence remaining in my memory is enough to bring the scene of that year vividly back to life.

Climbing Han Mountain and looking out, a long, winding, vast, and majestic Han River encircles the dense city of Chaozhou. The city, eager to leap, and the river, majestic and far-reaching, reflect each other in the mist and water, making the scenery as vivid as a beautiful woman dancing. Looking far into the distance, the sand is white on the southwestern side, and flocks of birds are playing. Below the beach and water is a bamboo forest, a large bamboo kingdom that sways all day long. That is a famous small island by the river, light and pure in appearance, with a sense of being detached from the world. Facing the bamboo forest from afar stands Ke Xi Pagoda, tall and majestic, lush and ancient, with a powerful aura that still strikes people even from a distance. Turning my eyes back, I look down at Xiangzi Bridge, neat, light, and beautiful, like a rainbow across the sky. The people on the bridge seem like objects in a wonderful painting, vaguely indistinct, yet coming steadily and going far away. Beside and under the bridge, on both sides of the river, green waves ripple like brocade, and boats play on the water, which cannot help but make one's mind wander. Slowly counting the scenery coming from Jiangdong, all the way to the foot of Han Mountain bordering the river, I sighed a sweet and comfortable sigh, and felt relaxed all over! Raising my head and focusing my gaze on the vast sky, a majestic wind blows towards my face, the spirit of youth leaps up, I shake my head and sing loudly, truly as if in a dream.

Stepping on green hills, grasping green trees, listening to birds singing, sitting in dense shade, stroking the clear stream that gurgles like music, I simply soak my feet, which, though I am a student, often like to wear wooden clogs, into the cool water, acting like a child, oblivious to the world! That is the soul of my youth, that is the beautiful dream of my teens!

After wandering around and getting tired, I linger to the dormitory, and the chime of the ancient temple to the left scatters elegantly in the quiet and beautiful foothills. This also reminds me of Han Yu's Han Wengong Temple on the mountain, which is why it is named Han Mountain. Stepping across Xiangzi Bridge and picking up the slanting stone steps to climb, the ancient temple stands majestically above, quietly accompanied by the gentle breeze, old pine trees, fragrant flowers, and various warbling birds on the black tile roof outside the wall. I love to sit on the cool stone in front of the temple, exposing my elegant chest, watching tourists, looking at Han Mountain, looking at Xiangzi Bridge, surrounded by a completely intoxicating and serene atmosphere. On the stone tablet beside the temple are the inscriptions of ancient people such as Han Yu and Su Dongpo, carved on the stone in deep black, vigorous, majestic, and ancient characters. From time to time, some foreigners even come to visit! Looking at the traces on the stone, I am immersed in the mood of reminiscing about the past.

Every summer night, the moonlight of Lingnan shines on the foothills of Han Mountain, and the interest of young people becomes even more unusually exuberant. The silvery white moonlight shines all over the deep, quiet mountain, under the trees, the elegant campus, the quiet and elegant old-style dormitory, the windows, and the houses, all adorned with intoxicating moonlight, making the scenery of the foothills of Han Mountain even more beautiful. Therefore, the fluttering and restless spirit will naturally leap into action. Stepping out of the dormitory door, strolling, sitting on a cool stone, under the trees and branches. Chasing after the beauty of the mountains that is blurred and about to melt in the distance, I never feel that it is almost midnight, but the interest is still strong. Then I lie down on the cool and sweet-smelling pavilion, sleeping boldly and freely, breathing in a clear and sweet taste that is so refreshing that it feels almost otherworldly. Sometimes, even though the moon has set in the west and the night is almost over, I am even more fascinated by the blurred colors!

Thinking of these things, I suddenly remember sleeping overnight at the foot of Han Mountain again last year. Although the scenery was the same as before, my heart was so scattered that it was not worth a glance at the face of Han Mountain. And after one night, I couldn't help but leave! That young heart has long been buried!

A Family Letter 188

— Ye Cheng

Brother, in our hometown, it must be the time when frogs are croaking everywhere in the green grass ponds.

It is said that the city is sensitive to the seasons. Yes, when the swallows return from the south, the streets playing jazz music are already flying the flags of summer sales. But don't the people in the countryside understand these things? Their lives are held in the grip of the seasons. When the migratory birds sing, they sow; now is what we habitually call the plum rain season, when rice seedlings should be transplanted. But reading in the newspaper that drought is looming everywhere, all the experience left by our hundreds of generations of ancestors is in vain.

I remember the image of returning home last year, in fact, it is reflected in my mind all the time; those fields were as hard as pig iron, and the sound of water pumping along the river almost never stopped. The riverbed was exposed like the white belly of a fish, but the fields seemed to be filled with mercury. When the plow hit the ground, it made a dull metallic sound, as unpleasant as an old man drinking too much wine. Every purplish face lost its expression, and angry arms were raised, holding the clay face of the "fierce general" god. At that time, the philanthropists in the city, thinking about the food problem for the coming year, finally brought out Zhang Tianshi to set up an altar and perform rituals. The children of the land, who understood the seasons, looked up at the scorching sun in the sky, and lived on sighs as if they were food.

"There is not a single ox in the countryside, but people are working like oxen!" When you shouted this, you almost looked like you were fighting an enemy. Now your voice and your shadow are floating before my eyes.

I feel very ashamed. Father thought that I was not a "farmer" and we took two different paths. Father's intention was naturally good, farmers will never amount to anything, but what about selling the ancestral property and cultivating me into a so-called "scholar" who graduated from middle school? It seems forgivable that I could not get promoted and make a fortune as my father had expected, but I have been struggling to fill my stomach for many years, and now I don't even have the courage to speak! Although scholars and farmers take two completely different paths, the result is that my father is completely disappointed.

But the previous generation knew how to accept adversity. When I returned home last year, Father still entrusted his dreamlike hope to me. He wanted me to be patient, old eagles have eyes, and scholars will always have their day! He repeated the story of the top scholar Lu to us under the kerosene lamp, smiling like that.

"There will always be a day to turn things around!" he concluded, puffing on his pipe hard.

Brother, at that time, I saw you rolling your bloodshot eyes, and I knew that you could no longer bear that kind of philosophy of "patience". But Father took patience as a "family motto", and our ancestors started from patience. Although Father didn't say a word when he saw me off on the boat that day,

Page 19

I knew that his only teaching, "patience," was about to burst out, but we parted in such silence. Perhaps he was not sure that "patience" was a successful creed.

The day after I received your letter, it rained, but the news of floods came again. Now the seasons are out of order, and the people in the countryside, who are held in the grip of the seasons, can no longer be patient. You said that the people who are working like oxen this year have abandoned the lessons inherited from their ancestors. In fact, all of this is in vain. Sensitive people in the city are thinking about how to help our rural areas! You might laugh out loud when you hear this news, right?

Movie News

Random Notes from Happy Forest 190

In the scene of "Little Aunt," Luo Jun and Xia Peizhen met for the first time through Ying Yin's introduction. Both were shy and speechless. Ying Yin urged them to talk. So, Luo Jun said:

"Sister! Do you have classes in the classroom?"

"Yes! Brother-in-law!" Xia Peizhen replied.

"Then, your school is closed on Sundays, right?"

"Yes!"

"Then, you eat lunch at noon?"

But Xia Peizhen couldn't help but laugh. Knocking on the teacup...

Zhang Lingling told her friend, "I got the best score on the social studies test this time, I got ninety-eight points!"

The friend said, "If I went to knock on this teacup, I could have done even better, isn't my strength a little greater than yours?" Teapot smashed...

Xu Suzhen can speak Cantonese. The fake Han Lagen, Zhao Tushan, asked him to teach: "Please teach me how to pronounce the three characters "Zhao Tushan" in Cantonese?"

The answer is: "Tea kettle (Zhao) broken (Tushan)!" Everyone then...

"Little Aunt" actor Yao Ping bought a two-cent loaf of bread and asked the shop assistant why the bread was smaller than before. The shop assistant said that the bread is small so it's more convenient for you to eat, so Yao Ping gave a cent and took the bread, saying, "Then, everyone is convenient, your counting price is also convenient."

"Jade Horse" is Thrilling and Exciting 191

"Jade Horse" is Xu Xinfu's first sound dialogue feature film, and is currently working day and night at the photography site, and will be completed soon. "Jade Horse" is a film with the anti-drug movement as its theme. The film depicts an organized drug manufacturing organization that manufactures a large number of drugs (his trademark is a pair of jade horses). Detective Wang Tiemin is the strongest opponent of drug prohibition. He uses all means and goes through countless hardships, and finally cracks this "jade horse" trademarked drug manufacturing organization. The set design is by Dong Tianya. This features bizarre and tortuous secret room tunnels, and magnificent new-style buildings. The magnificence of the set is also a feature of the film. The overall atmosphere is full of adventure and excitement, and will undoubtedly refresh the audience.

Hu Die and "Tuberose" 192

Since Hu Die went abroad, our movie audiences have not enjoyed Hu Die's new works for a long time. Her recent works before she went abroad were the sound dialogue film "Tuberose," written and directed by Cheng Bugao. That film was as beautiful and elegant as a flower with a subtle fragrance. Because of Hu Die's departure, the film has not yet been completed. Now that Ms. Hu is on her way back to the country, then, not long after, we can see the moving performance of this artist called "genius" in "Tuberose."

Introducing "Nostalgia" 193

Shen Xiling, known for his two films, "Women's Cry" and "Shanghai Twenty-Four Hours," his third creation, "Nostalgia," is now being screened at the Xin Guangda Theater.

In "Women's Cry," because it was his first time directing, he could not fully use his artistic skills, but the audience could almost clearly see the superiority of the young director's skills. The premiere of "Shanghai Twenty-Four Hours" fully demonstrated his artistic genius and his just exposure of dissatisfaction with reality. The technique of contrasting the rich and the poor truly touched people's hearts.

This time, Shen Xiling, with his righteous poet's emotion, entrusted his infinite grief for his motherland in "Nostalgia." The entire film is full of exuberant passion, like a poignant and generous epic—this film is dubbed and shot, starring Xuan Jinglin, Gao Qianping, Sun Min, Zhao Dan, Mei Xi, and others.

Zhou Hu's Paris 195

Paris Communication: Zhou Jianyun and Hu Die have traveled to various European countries and have now arrived in Paris a few days ago. On the second day of their arrival, Chinese compatriots in France held a grand welcome party for them at the Paris Chinese Student Association. After the chairman gave a welcome speech, Hu Die stood up to give a reply. Zhou Jianyun gave a brief report on their trip abroad. Zhou's conversation was interspersed with a few jokes from time to time, which always caused laughter throughout the venue. After the meeting, a public banquet was held for Zhou Hu at the Wanhua Building. They were then led to the nearby Luxembourg Gardens to take pictures and dispersed happily. According to Zhou, they must stay in Paris for two or three days, and then go to London, Rome, and other places. When they leave Europe, it will be around June 15th, and it may not be until the beginning of July that they can return to their motherland.

"Autumn Fan Bright Lamp" 196

The film "Autumn Fan Bright Lamp" is the latest production of Lianhua Film Company, with all dubbing and singing. The plot in the film has a long process, events of the past ten years or so, which become strange changes after ten years. With complex plots on many sides, it constitutes a situation of sorrow and joy. Streams converge, in an orderly manner. The director, Tan Youliu, has a strong spirit and performs in a well-organized manner, and the strength of the drama is undoubtedly increased. The control of the actors in the whole drama is also very suitable. Li Lili plays from her girlhood to her middle age. Each period can be considered in detail. Li herself said, "Since acting in films, this film is the most laborious." She is known for playing young girls, but now she also has excellent achievements in playing middle-aged women. A capable person can naturally do everything. Diao Banhua, as a new actor, first showed her skills in "New Woman" and showed her talent. She plays an important role in this film. Even a small test of her skills is already outstanding, and her future will be limitless. Other actors such as Gu Menghu, Jiang Junchao, and Han Lagen all have special achievements. In short, this film, whether in terms of plot, direction, or actors, proves its greatness everywhere. In addition to the beautiful music and singing, it adds a lot of color to this film.

Who is Your Lifeline? 197

Li Lili was preparing to record the song for "Autumn Fan Bright Lamp", and the song "You Are My Lifeline" was constantly humming in her mouth all day long. Sitting "You Are My Lifeline," walking "You Are My Lifeline" holding a newspaper is also "You Are My Lifeline," eating wontons is also "You Are My Lifeline," it's simply "Lifeline" everywhere. Therefore, Diao Banhua, who is inseparable from her, couldn't help but laugh, "Really like a madman, who is your lifeline?" Banhua asked like this, which was very interesting, and immediately made Li Lili's face fly up with a few red clouds.
